O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	I, my very dear son, have completed this book for you, which is the end of the science of medicine along with its fulfillment, and have finished it by its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I will complete this for you with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forbidden in our region and is entirely unknown everywhere, the science and craft are perishing and decaying, and nothing remains of it from foreign lands except for small descriptions of the ancients that the hands have corrupted.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this (cause), errors and vanities have come, and intentions are closed and wisdom is driven away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	 I seem to wish to bring it to life together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition, declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And I shall come with the forms of the iron cauteries, and other instruments of work together with the arrangement of their declaration and preparation as required.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good master of hand is found in our times, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who undertakes it should be summoned in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of limbs, and their shapes and joints and separations thereof, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and marrow and the number of bones, and the movement and the resting places and the veins moving and the stationary ones, and the location of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	 And for this reason Hippocrates said that the name without the work is nothing;
et meismement en l’art de main.	 and especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not skilled in the things mentioned above, let him beware lest he err and kill men.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 As I have often wished for many who engage in this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	 I saw a madman who lanced an abscess of scrofulas from a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of her neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	 And I saw another madman who removed a stone from an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut it he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	 And I saw another madman who took care of our land's duke who had his leg broken, and with the breakage he had a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	 and the ignorant madman straightened the break over the wound with strong pressure, and did not leave salve on the wound, and left it thus incomplete.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	 And command him not to dislocate it.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And keep the leg until it has completely swollen and the feet have come to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	 I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and dislocate the leg.
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 And when I had dislocated it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	 But the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and it could not heal it.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 And the corruption did not stop going through the member until all the limb was completely destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And it is necessary for another person to flatten an abscess and then burn it through the evil of his power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is pure of black bile, it should not be touched with iron if it cannot be completely removed from that place where the corruption is.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	 Therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two categories.
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	 namely, surgery where there is danger in many ways;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And I will show in every part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	 Therefore it is necessary that you protect yourself, so that the foolish fool cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	 Take your arms in custody, and begin with your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	 And leave the incurable diseases of great sickness;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 And remove your arms from that which causes doubt in you, and be vigilant within yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	 Galen said in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Do not treat an evil disease lest you be called a foolish healer.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	 The first chapters are about fire cauterization and the cauterization of medicinal diseases, and these chapters are ordered from head to feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 and the forms of instruments, the irons for cauterization, and everything else that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	 The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and about blistering and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 and these chapters are ordered and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	 The third chapters are about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 and these are ordered from head to feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, remembering the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	 I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest and most subtle words and secret responses.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	 and on this topic spoke many wise men and agreed with it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 and they supported my words, for I shall shorten them.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	 I say that cautery helps universally to all constitutions where there is matter, whether it be one or two constitutions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 this means warm constitution with matter and dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	 In a warm and dry constitution along with matter, some said and declared that cautery is of great help:
et li autre dirent le contraire:	 and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 that cautery does not help in disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	 Because the nature of fire is hot, it should not be used to cure a hot disease with heat or dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 and he who said the opposite, that cautery provides great help to a hot and dry disease that comes in men's chests.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of a man and his moisture according to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it sometimes through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	 And in all ways, do not interfere except for those who have experienced it and who know through long use the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and causes of illness, and their symptoms and the duration and time span.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 We are not afraid of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all men should conform and agree to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery together with fire is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not go beyond the member that is burned, and it does no harm to another member unless named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	 Burning medicines come from one member to another when dislocated, causing illness of great healing to the member;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	 And by chance, the patient dies.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 The fire due to its high temperature and the goodness of its substance does not burn if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	 I have found this through experience and the length of my service and study in the art, and it is above truth in matters.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	 And because of this I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for it does not please me to reveal the secret of fire and the quality of the work, how it extinguishes diseases from bodies, as the philosopher says in demonstration.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	 Or accept it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauteries should be done and chose companions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	 And I say that the fire cautery is appropriate at all times because the harm occurring is kept under control by the aid of the fire cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And similarly, if the cautery is necessary because of severe pain, it should be done immediately before any greater harm comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	 Do not ever think, dear child, as foolish people do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	 for the disease that is cured by cautery will have no return;
et il le dient ensi;	 and they say so.
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 But it is not as they think, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion, dries up the humors that cause pain, and is more effective than medicine due to its speed of action and the power of its work and its dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	 And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its nature.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	 And in him are accumulated the superfluidities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered where there is little superfluidity and moisture, as cauterizations for pain, and such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	 But this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	 And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the rear of medicine, and it is indeed so.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 But they do not believe that cauterizations are effective after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauterizations are the rear of medicine because when we administer means of treatment for any disease and they do not work, then we administer cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is appropriate to know that cauteries are at the rear of medicine, not only according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	 The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are softened more than iron, and they did not say this except for the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	 and said that the lead of the cautery does not cause pustulation, but this is not true because I have proven it, and found that it is true in some men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 and cauteries made of gold are softer than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	 And even when you heat an instrument made of gold, you do not know when it is heated by the color of the gold, and it may suddenly cool.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	 and if you heat it too much;
si font au feu;	 it makes fire.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 And thus there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery, which we have found appropriate for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered you this chapter about the head from the neck to the feet, because the path will be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for both moist and dry conditions on the skull, and it is used to treat a disease known as "soda," as well as various humors that descend from the head into the eyes, ears, and cause many dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and also for all diseases caused by coldness, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	 The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by soluble medicine for 3 to 4 days depending on his condition and the potency, duration, and accustomed tolerance of the sickness.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 and then apply the hot iron to the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	 Then make him sit crosswise between your hands, place his hands on a flat surface.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	 After that, lay the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 Where your thumbs meet, if it bleeds there, heat the cautery called 'olivare', this is its form.
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	 And place it on its joint marked with ink, and do so by drawing and straining your hand little by little while twisting.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	 Then straighten your hand immediately, and return the joint if you see the bone protruding.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	 And if you don't see it, start the cautery again until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	 After taking a piece of linen cloth, put it wet and soft cotton inside, place it on the joint, and leave it for 3 days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	 Then cover it with moistened wool.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 Leave it until the burn is removed.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmacon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	 And as the ancients said, when an injury remains open for longer, it drains more.
et por ce si aide mues.	 and therefore helps heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And said one of them that the fire cautery should be left until part of the bone is burned, and then heal the one who was burned from the bone, and it should be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	 And others say that the cautery should be applied as much as possible, and pressed so hard that it forces out the bone as wide as a woman's thimble, because the fluids escape more easily.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	 and the wound must be kept open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 afterwards it should be cured and bandaged.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	 And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good in all cases, except for certain men who are fearful.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	 and I seem to leave it alone.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	 because the head is weakened by continuous liquids of nature, as we have witnessed in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And the same applies when the shoulder of the patient is weak by nature, and the first sign of cautery is more beneficial and healing for me, and from this use I have found salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of ancient pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	 When chronic and lasting pain comes in the head, it is necessary for the patient to use earwax and pills called "cochie", and purge of the head and oils and plasters.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 and if he is given the cautery as we have said before, it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	 Be careful that the patient's shoulder is of strong nature, and it should not be too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Then cauterize below that cautery a small amount as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	 After performing a fire cautery on each horn of the skull up to the bone, as previously mentioned, and perform the cautery called "vasselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	 and the area where vacuum bellows are placed.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	 and press your hand so that you do not see up to the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	 the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about it later.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 and the cauterization of the horns should be more delicate than that of the middle part of the head, and this is the form.
dou cautere dou chief	on the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	 When sudden pain comes in one part of the head and the disease spreads to the eye, and the head is purged with divers medicines, and other treatments that I have mentioned in the section on diseases are performed, but none of it helps:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 Then make cauteries according to two methods, namely of hot medicines and of fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	 For the cautery of hot medicines, take an alum stone, remove its bark and cover one end of it with wax, then apply it to the area where the pain is located in such a manner that you can place the alum stone underneath the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	 And when it is reset, let it stay properly and leave it like that for 12 hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	 Then remove the splint and apply garlic oil to the wound and leave it as it is for 2 or 3 days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 then place cotton soaked in butter over it until it becomes soft.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After the ointment is applied, let it heal.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 If you see fit, use some of the burning remedies I have written about or treat with 10 of the burning remedies I have written about.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The fire cautery is such as this.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cauterization tool in the shape of this [mold/form].
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	 It is called "closed" because the wound resembles a small container or cup shape.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	 Place it on the painful spot and hold your hand firmly over it, gently press it for a short while until half the thickness of the coal is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 And lift your hand so that the arteries do not burn, which are away from it, and draw out an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	 Put cotton on it in linen cloth and leave it there for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then put a damp cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 And if you want to burn out this abscess with the cautery called "cultellare", at its tip, be careful not to pierce the artery in this abscess which is not old.
de emigraine	From migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	 When treating an abscess as we have said before in the treatment of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauteries mentioned by the medicine do not help, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	 And so, on the side of the joint, draw a line half a thumb's length long, and then press once with your hand, holding back so as not to touch the artery nor reach the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	 And watch the jaw that becomes paralyzed when one eats, and let the nerves have no gaze but at the paralysis and that spasms do not come to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut or fear should arise in great measure, especially for those who are not familiar with it and untrained.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	 And leave the operation in its course;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it should be in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And if you see that this cautery does not help the illness and the patient is suffering, cauterize it near the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	 if you see that the artery extraction is necessary and it requires a cautery with two blades.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of cold ears
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the ear brings pain from cold and medicines soluble and other treatments mentioned in the division have been applied but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "poins", as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	 After pointing all around the sick ear, or both sides where the pain is, move a little away from the root of the ear after you have marked the spot.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	 and have ten points around each ear.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat the spot until it heals.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	 Torture to be cured by fire cautery is not applicable except for those that move due to flux, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 And do not perform a cautery on similar conditions arising from scabs and nerves swellings.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	 When treating this condition of torture that moves due to flux of eyes, head purges and gargles, it is not worth it; therefore you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	 One in the root of the ear, another slightly further from the temple, and the third near the junction of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	 and place the cautery in the healthy part of it, and make him cauterize towards the top of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as far as a thumb.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	 Leave the cautery for as long as half of the coal is burning.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	 And it resembles the form of a surgeon's knife that we have shown earlier, but it is slightly more delicate and the blade should be somewhat thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After treating the shoulder as I previously stated, let it heal when it is sound.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	 When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	 One on each of the two forehead horns, one at the neck, and one where the arm is called "waste" as we have previously stated, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 And let it be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	diarrhea (from Latin lithargyrios, meaning "stone-like")
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	 For this disease, give the patient large iris-like seeds or round pills made of brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	 Afterward, anoint the head of the patient entirely, and place a plaster made of mustard seed or mustard treatment on the occiput (the back part of the skull).
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	 And this is the method of cauterization:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 If you do it as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	 If it is purged like this, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	 And if it isn't, perform three fire cauterizations on the neck down to the collarbone, leaving a space of one inch between each.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	 and treat it as others, and if you see that it is getting better, and the patient can bear it, perform one fire cauterization;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if necessary, two more on the temples, and treat it until it is purged;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 And let the cauterization called "olive" be as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 The head should be purified for years and as we have said before.
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	 After the head of the patient, then make a fire cautery on the head and on each horn, and also three on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	 And if needed, and the body is wet and the patient is suffering, and the illness is far advanced, make four fire cauteries on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	 and let it burn until the deeper part is seared, then remove your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 Then treat until it heals, and the cautery called "olivare" which we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for the phlegmatic one, and it is first necessary to clean the brain for years and other treatments as we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffering from thinking about taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	 And if it is an infant who cannot bear it, give a gargle and make it chew softening medicine for the brain frequently with good foods.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	 After the king's head in the middle, do as previously said, and apply the fire cautery on the servant, and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if the patient is outside and suffering, apply cauterization as I have said to him who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let the cauterization be olive oil according to the method that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, apply a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy, the superfluidities or corrupted and putrid humors produce thick phlegm, then apply cauteries with such cauterizations as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the excesses are declining towards melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moist, then give them to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what was stated earlier in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	 After the king's head of the patient.
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	 After that, make a linen tourniquet well made, like a circle, and put it on his head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	 And the patient should be crosswise, and tightly bound from all sides.
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	 After that, apply lime to the wound, using old goat's milk.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	 And the fire must be heated moderately, so that it can be endured by the patient.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	 After vacuuming the circle from within the head, let it cool.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And have this done to the patient once a week with good management, until he is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 Or, if you wish to cauterize it, make points all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	 This method of cauterization reduces the brain significantly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 Then place wet, soft cotton on top with butter and linseed oil.
de l’awe des eulz	Of the eyes (lit. of the hairs)
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes (lit. hairs) come first according to the signs that I have said in the division, then start and give the patient something cleansing for the head, and guard it from all moisture, and let it sweat or bathe many times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	 After instructing the patient to lie on his back, perform the cauterization in the head and perform two cauterizations on each temple where there is a single opening or an opening on one side only.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	 And apply the entire cauterization to all veins and arteries that are under the skull, and let them be long according to the width of the temple.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 And beware of bleeding, and if you see too much blood flowing out, stop it with your power as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	 I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incision of cautery how to apply it.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 Sometimes they make a cauterization or an instrument beneath the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	for the removal of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	 When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed to be above the veins or in the area of the arteries near the forehead;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	 and one sees that it is cold phlegmatic superfluidities, then do the cauterization as I said at the beginning of the work descending on the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	 I cauterize in the head, two cauterizations on the two temples, and two cauterizations or instruments beneath the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 And if it is necessary more, then cauterize carefully on top of the mole with the smallest cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The body weeps tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	 When treating according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three colds infusions (to drink).
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	 After the king's head (the boil), do a fire or olive oil cauterization.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	 Do two cauteries called "clavilis" on the two moles, a little under the hair.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 And beware of the artery that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize this cautery which is called "olive oil.
de coi ci est li forme:	 Of this matter are the forms:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	 If you see, then do two cauteries on the two moles as long as the moles are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And don't leave the hand unless the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pricks the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	 Sometimes, the hairs of the eyelashes are converted into sweat glands and prick the eye, and then fire cautery is performed according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 (This refers to) fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	 For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	 When they have grown and are even, then put the patient in a safe place;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	 after that, on top of the eyelashes, make a mark with paper like the shape of the thistle flower, and make the start of the sign along the hairs.
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Then put softened cotton soaked in egg white and pepper mint oil on it, then heat the cautery according to this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	 After heating the cautery repeatedly at the specified place, the tip should be burned.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	 And the signs of the success of the work are that you see the paper withdrawn and the hairs raised at the tip of the oil.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 Then lower your hand, leave it like that for three days, then put softened cotton in butter until the burn is healed.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	 And if hairs grow later and the paper becomes soft, then repeat the cauterization on that same spot, just as you did before.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if the hairs are falling out, cauterize it until the paper is raised to its natural position and is even, and do not prick the hairs with oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	 The burn cure is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a paper in the shape of the myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	 Then take French soap and live coal, one ounce each, grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	 and heat it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you made like a myrtle leaf, and put the hot mixture on the hairs.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	 and if the patient is affected only in the oil, it should be treated only there, and if in both places as well;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	 And put cotton wool soaked in oil under an eggshell.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The patient's shoulder should be kept healthy and put your hand on top of the medication, and press the affected area and move it whenever the patient feels a bite from the medicine as it feels like a burn.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have made it [the patient] stay still for a long time, give him medicine to his body.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	 And when the bite has passed, lift the affected area and observe if you see the paper raised as it was raised by constriction from fire or incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 If it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	 If not, replace the medication on the affected area or the medication has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes are steady.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then place cotton wool soaked in butter on it until the blisters are healed, afterwards, apply the ointment called "diaphensis" and others until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you need to be careful with your work so that the medicine does not stick to the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	 If the paper becomes soft afterwards and the hairs prick in the oil, then repeat the medicine on that spot which has been properly prepared, just like you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And this is the shape of the feather of the vervain:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	 Know that human eyes vary in size and according to their size, this shall be your constraint.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And do not deviate from the straight path for those who are engaged in this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When curing a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cures are not helpful, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	 Instruct the patient to place their head on a pillow.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	 And hold the sick person's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or lower its head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	 Then put a soft cotton cloth inside an eggshell or under parchment on the oil.
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	 After heating the iron rod (cautery) to a certain point:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	 And position the head so that it forms a V shape, with the iron rod placed at the base of the V.
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	 If you see, it should be aligned from one head to the other, and if you see, it should also be like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 However, the position of the head as described is good for your purpose.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	 After opening the fistula if it is open, drain the pus, and dry it.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	 If it is closed, then you should open it, and draw out the excrement (or perhaps 'pus' in this context).
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	 Afterwards put the hot iron cauter on the nipple area under the oil (be careful not to burn yourself).
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 Heat the iron cauter in the oil fat and let it rot.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you perform the cautery right up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	 If that does not work, try heating the iron cauter again if necessary, and leave it for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	 Afterwards place damp cotton in butter and apply the drying ointment until it heals. If after forty days it is not healed, apply a corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 And the king, according to what he comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And here is a method of cauterization for fistula that none of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	 To the fistula, make an incision and open it;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 After placing the camahan (substance) in the incision from this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	 and they place as much as a cubit of wax;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	 Hold your hand with the camahan firmly, and the patient must not move at all, until the wax melts and runs to its oil;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	 And it is necessary that you put cotton soaked in egg oil on the patient's wound.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 The wax will heal the fistula and the wound by marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 If the fistula is healed by the cauterization as we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, it is necessary to administer purgatives to the nose and return the fistula to the body of the nose as required in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cavities in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often cavities occur in lips, which are called "hairs," and similarly in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When treating these cavities as mentioned in the previous section and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cautery spatula according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	 Put it quickly into those cavities until it reaches the bottom;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the shoulder of scab until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	From the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	 When pus comes to the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth, after it forms a pustule and grows and becomes a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	 And you cure it as we have said in other parts, but it does not help at all.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	 Then it is necessary that you use the fire cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	 After pouring or puncturing the fistula, keep your hand until the iron becomes hot at its base and at its tip.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do it once or twice, after curing what we have said in treatments, until it is healthy.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	 And if it is treated in this way, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 If not, you must find the joint and remove the rotten bone, as per what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	toothache
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	 When the gums become soft due to moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it is of no avail, then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	 After applying the heated iron, let the shape come out as it will, and you place a chain on the tooth in this manner.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	 Insert the heated iron quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat approaching the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	 After you let go, repeat the process according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 After filling the patient's mouth with salt water, let it remain for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the moving teeth are held firm and the softened gums are kept restricted, and the corrupt moisture dries out.
de la dolor des dens	of the tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	 When toothache due to cold comes from either frostbite or fever, and the treatments with medicines are of no use, then it is necessary to apply cautery according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 and cautery of butter and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	 The cautery of butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and its end in an iron or copper spoon.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	 Then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent peg, dip it in boiling butter, and place it on the painful tooth immediately and hold until it becomes cool.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 And do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that wool and cotton in cold butter are moistened, place them on the diseased tooth and hold hot iron on it until the heat comes to the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	 The cautery combined with fire is such that you take a dog chain of iron or steel, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	 After heating the cautery, its shape will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 Do this often, for the pain will be relieved that very same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	 The patient must fill his mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then blow hard.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 This is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	 And make the cautery in any shape you want, and according to what you are able.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And this is the form of a dog:
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	 When scrofula is of a cold and moist flushes, and not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire-cautery from what follows, and have it openings for the smoke to issue to the cautery on the other side.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	 And place the hot cautery on the abscess once, where it is needed, until it reaches the opening of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	 And if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess and leave it thus for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	 Place dampened cotton on top until the pus is drained out.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the joint of ulcers and abscesses until it is sound.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the arm:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	 When worms attack on the channels of the womb, and particularly when it comes from a cold constitution, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first with soluble medicines.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 Afterwards make the fire cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to come up to the throat, and do not dare to go deep but a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	 Afterwards make the other fire cautery at the junction of the neck to the head of the spine, and let it be the cautery called "clavicle" from which we have the shape before.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And heal the joint as we have said before until it is sound.
de la toust	When moisture conquers over the channels of the throat (toust), and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then the patient should be purged first with soluble medicines; afterwards do cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go up to the throat, but a little. Afterwards do .i. other cautery at the jointure of the neck to the head of the spine (col au chief de l'espinee), and let the cauteries which is called "clavile" have the shape as before; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healthy.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	 When all and the disease of gout are of cold humors, and the patient has neither fever nor sweating, and the disease is old, make two fire cauterizations on the forearm veins.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	 and another cautery in the groin between the testicles;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 and let the cautery called "clavicle" according to the shape as previously described be used.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	 And if you wish, do cautery by pricking all over the cautery called "point" as described in the disease of ears (previously);
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 and the points be up to 30, or within that area.

Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And since the cauterizations are lighter because you do them in pairs of two.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	 Afterwards, make the patient lie down on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	 After taking the key which is within the titillete with your left hand.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 And if the jointure is dislocated within, heat the cautery which has two nerves as shown here:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	 And cauterize (the affected area) until it pierces through the skin, and four figures of the cautery will appear.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	 And thus, a cautery with three prongs is used for this purpose, because the figures of cauterization are called cauteries.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 And these prongs correspond to the fineness of a tent and this is the shape of the cautery with three prongs:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is twisted around this nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	 After placing the cautery on, break it with silk.
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 After putting the patient to rest, let not the limbs be moved for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 If it is dislocated upwards, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery rod or many cauteries while pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 For the joint is set back in place, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When there are coldness and much moisture in the stomach that harms its constitution, and the catarrh multiplies for him, and in the usual methods of treatment it does not help; therefore the patient should lie on his back, extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	 Then three cauteries are placed under the spoon of the scoop at the width of a thumb, the entire cautery must be clavile (driven in), and two cauteries outside each side so that the figures of the cauteries are at three angles, and with enough space between one and another that they are not joined together when they spill pus.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 And let the cauteries be so sharp that they pierce both parts of the flesh, and let the figure of the cauteries be in accordance with this shape:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	 And if you wish to cauterize within the stomach using a large cautery in this shape:
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	 and he who fears the cautery, cauterize by pressing and applying it on top of the stomach at the point according to the quantity you wish to burn:
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 then cauterize completely with the cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the treatment of the wound that we had before, let it heal when it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	 When the liver experiences pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, it is expelled from its natural condition due to excesses:
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	 and the patient is cured of what has been said earlier in the divisions, but it does not help him, and he must be attentive to his bedding:
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	 And sign the third cautery according to this form and this shape and this quantity above the liver, remove the hypochondriacs, where the cost of the ribs comes.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	 And there should be distance between each cautery equal to the thickness of a thumb.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	 And let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press too hard with your hand on all the cauteries.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	 And only burn half of the ear, and let the patient lie straight on his feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	 If he cannot, then let him lie down, extend his legs, and lift his arms.
et c’est li forme:	 And this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	 If you wish, you can perform these cauteries with the scalpel, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn too deeply, for you will singe all of the body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And it shall not reach boiling, for the herb is very subtle in that place, and the wise can see it.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	 When you have an abscess in the liver, and you want to know whether it is within the liver's flesh or its membrane.
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	 If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not very strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 And if it is in the membrane, it feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	 And when this treatment ceases for the patient, it is necessary that he be on guard over his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 and then hold down the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a flat iron, as shown in this figure:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	 Heat the cautery until the corners are burning, and come up to where the pus is, so that it can be completely removed;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After the treatment according to the treatment of abscesses until it heals;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And this cautery should not be used by anyone without extensive study in the art of medicine, for many times these diseases have been aggravated by it.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can operate boldly, but I think it is better to wait a little longer.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	 The ancients said that one should make cauterizations for pleurisy with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	 take a long root of aristolochia, the largest one you can find, and it should be dry, and as thick and long as your thumb.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	 and wet the root in oil, heat it on fire, and cauterize the cautery between the armpit and neck, and apply a few small cauteries downwards in the area below the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	 and the cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining slightly behind.

et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 And do not press your hand forcefully, but open it gently as when sniffing.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	 And an old man said that anyone using the fire-cautery resembles a razor, and they heat it and put it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And then the pain jumps wildly, as we said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mice, that is as we have said in the division of cures and it does not help at all, then apply three ways of cautery, all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	 Of these methods, it is that you make three or four cauterizations in a line according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver-cautery that we have said before.
