et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	 And hold your hand away from the continuation of both jaws, and each wound should be of the size of three fingers joined together.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 and prepare a piece of sponge and a lot of cloth for wiping the blood, then insert the sharpened spatula of two parts as shown here.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	 from the incision which is below the temple up to the second incision.
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 and cut out all the fat that is between the two fissures to its entire length, which is above the bone, then continue from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then remove this sharpened spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	insert the instrument called "culter" (which is pointed on one side and soft, not pointed, and its shape is:)
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And cut the bone obliquely towards the skin according to your knowledge, and the bone is soft towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the mid-incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	 And cut all the eyelashes that descend from the head until the incision is continuous up to where the opening of the eyeball appears, and then further proceed in the middle split up to the other eyelid.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	 Then draw equal amounts of blood and press on the place where the blood was taken.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	 then put a tent of old cotton in each split and place damp cloths soaked in wine, oil and vinegar on top, and ensure that pus does not come.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and on the third day loosen the ligature, and bring a strong plant of cold water, then apply a basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	the removal of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	 When someone commonly comes with an acute catarrh, and you see the eyes becoming swollen and small, and clouding vision, and burned papers.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	 And the hair falls out, and if one presses on the head in pain, and the patient coughs.
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 Therefore, learn through these symptoms that those matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the medicine to be used for it, if it is there, should be applied.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you shall tell the patient to bend his head back, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another wide one in the cheek.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	 And begin at the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	 and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating.
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	 and when the bone is exposed, drain all the blood with a sponge, then loosen between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton and linen thread.
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	 Then lay above it cloths soaked in wine and oil, and keep away from getting hot.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 When it is removed (a tumor or foreign body), you should rub the bone until tender flesh begins to grow, then heal with drying agents that promote healing.
En teil maniere:	 In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	 Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster with them.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 And apply it to these wounds to stop the pain everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear stoppage (stopping/blockage of the ears)
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	 Everything that falls in ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	 or grain, or beast, or stone from the mine, or similar things like iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	 or seeds, such as peas, beans, lentils.
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 or something flowing, such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear stone or another thing that does not fit into the ear, does not lie in the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	 If you see the stone, distill some purple oil or camphor oil, then apply extraction.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	 And you make him cough with condys, and stop his nostrils when coughing comes, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	 And stretch the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	 Many times comes fever due to this treatment.
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if it does not come with fever, bring about the extraction of small tweezers, here is the form for it:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	 If it leaps with tweezers, that is good.
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	 if not, bring about the extraction of an onion-shaped fine probe of small thickness.
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	 and if it does not leap with that, make a bee-shaped cane and push the head of the cane or ear perforation strongly, and stop the one who is around the cane with wax so that air cannot enter with the cane.
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	 then draw it out in form, for many times comes fever as we have said.
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	 And if it does not come forth in such a manner, it takes glue from what it takes the birds, and puts on some instrument that is sharp for this purpose, and puts a little cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	 And if it does not jump out of all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear so that pus comes in and it spasms;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	 and the method of cutting is that you make the patient first drain the head, and draw out the blood according to the measure of its strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	 And make the cut as round as a moon until you reach the bone, then break it according to your strength, and suck out the juice quickly with your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And heal it while it is still draining pus.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	 And if there are grains (pus) swelling up, administer extraction (incision or lancing).
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 And if it cannot drain, apply a thin, subtle sponge according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 make an incision of that grains.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	 But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist due to ear moisture, as long as you have made many cuts.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 Then take out with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extractions align.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In water that falls into the ear, the patient should use warm gargles of first remedies, and fill the ear with large cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on that same ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out because of that, it's good. (This line refers to the cotton in the ear staying in place.)
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	 if this is not done, take many stones according to the length of your thumb and light, and heat them slightly with fire.
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	 and place the patient or wounded person with his ear, and boil water on one side of it. From the other side, take another stone and strike the stone in the ear with it.
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	 and do not stop hitting one stone against the other until the water boils completely out, and then it will burst out.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	 And if you see, grab the string, and push one of the shoulders into the ear, and take hold of the other head with fire until the more tender joint is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 then straighten the joints of the other limbs until the pain subsides completely, as we have said in the previous section.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	 In the extraction of the beast, if it has a small body, like a flea and similar creatures, treat it as we have said in the classification;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	 but if it has a large body that can be felt, bring forth the extraction of tweezers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 and it is the lighter things to remove that are in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	 In the removal of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the classification and the treatment of distillation, and the treatment does not help, then you must observe the ear in the sun;
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 If there are any openings (wounds), draw them shut with fine forceps if they do not close by themselves. And if they do not open, take the cord that is in the form mentioned here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	 And put the smaller plier (tweezers) in the ear according to the amount of pain the patient has, then press firmly on the cord.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 Do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	 And if they do not obey to come out, stop the cord of cotton around it as I said before.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	 And if they do not come out as we said before, administer distillations that the ancients have proved to be effective in the treatment of worms. You will find it or how to treat with distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if you distill your oil and medicines into the ear with this instrument, here is its form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	 The lower part should be of silver or brass, narrow and pointed, with a cover above for distilling.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	 And for pressing within the distillation, use an instrument made of brass that is suitable, and if you see, take the scraper and wrap it around the tip with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	 Then pour your oil or juice into the canal, and whatever you see of your medicines in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	 Then push the scraper into the cotton and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or the ear moves.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	 And the patient feels pain within, and it should be distilled [treated] with fire in the same way as it is distilled in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And ensure that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear stoppage (stopping/blockage of the ears)
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	 No child is born without some deformity in the ears.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	 And this same thing happens in men by the stoppage of a wound or pus born within the ear, and sometimes it comes all the way into the ear if one cannot see it.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 And sometimes the deformity turns outwards, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	 Therefore, if it comes all the way into the ear and one cannot see it, it is a difficult cure in many ways, and in this case you must place the sick person's ear in the sun.
et regarde dedens:	 And look within:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 If you see the opening apparent, perform entirely this spatula of which form is given here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	 And be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear.
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 If the opening is from cartilage or corrosion of the ear, hold it with subtle tweezers and strike gently until all the cartilage is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the tumor has invaded fully into the ear, take a sharp, thin scissors and heat it slightly in fire, then insert it into the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	 If you feel an opening that causes the patient pain in the ear, make a gentle puncture and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 Then place a wick in the ear according to the size of the wound and moist it with the Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	 Apply this every day until the wound heals, or take a linen cloth and moisten it in strong vinegar, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top of it.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 And if you see an ear swelling, then you should pull the linen cloth away and move another linen cloth moistened with rose oil and beeswax until the swelling is removed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal it until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, then place it on the ear, and use other treatments to stop the bleeding which are either cauterization or distillation treatments.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of paper (meaning "skin")
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	 This is the treatment for blisters that come in paper when they are moist and dry. Then you should stretch them with pliers and forceps, and scrape them from their roots with a spatula.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 Then put broken vitriol on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	 And if [the patient] does not cut it open, the cautery with the fine lenticular cautery should be used, and after the incision is made, the cauterization is beneficial.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	 And many times they repair themselves, but nothing remains of their roots.
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 and when they are cauterized by fire, the roots are burned and they do not return.
de la gresle	Of the hail (meaning "hardened lumps under the skin")
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	 Many times come in paper from the eyes something that appears like hail in its shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "hail", and it is a thick accumulation of moisture in the upper and lower paper (eye).
li ovraiges est telz:	 The works are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	 Take care if the swelling remains silent from both sides, it is an easy thing to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Then (you) open (it), next, peel the skin from both sides lightly, then take it with the forceps and crush it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	 if you cannot crush it without piercing a little paper, do not worry the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 and if the wound is large, join it with stitches and cure it until it heals.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 and if it is small, do not apply force, for the oil will restore it soon and add heat to the wound.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	 If the swelling is descending within the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, hold the swelling with forceps and crush and press it from both sides.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	 And if the paper is dislocated by an incision, it causes no harm.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And when the hail is struck, boil oil of brackish water, and heal the wound of those who are injured by the hail until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	 Exinach is a grease that is injured in the skin of papers above, and this happens more often with children than with adults, and it causes them great discomfort, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot bear to look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 And because of this, they lie on their faces immediately and sleep on them, and their papers are wet under their eyelids with the exinach that has spread in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel something exit between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	 And the manner of work is that the patient places their head on a pillow;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	 then take the linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the size that contains external pus from each part, then place it over [the affected area];
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	 and press with your hands on both sides so that the pus is collected in the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	 then make a hole in the moisture with the narrow lancet, and it should not be larger than the wound made during vein opening.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	 and cut the skin completely so that you can see the pus;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 and in various positions, pus comes out of the hole, according to the shape of a white lard piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	 Take then a single piece of coarse cloth between your hands and spread it out; turn your hand from right to left until it is spread out.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 and ensure that you do not add anything in the slit, that you do not bring the spatula to the oil or pierce it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	 And if the dislocation does not open at the beginning of the slit, raise the slit slightly so that it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 Then reset it as we have said, then wet cloths in oil and water, and put them on the joint, and hold with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if such men who grind linen and put it on top to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess hot to the joint comes, then heal it with plasters soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	hair from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	 When paper-like growths grow with hairs, other than their nature, and are nourished, they harm the eyes and bring on diseases such as regular weeping and softening of the paper-like growths and albumin, to the point that it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	 And the cure is according to four ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 or by cautery with fire, or by cold medication as described in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by canines, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	 You must put the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of oil on your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	 if it is turned over, that's good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	 if not, push an awl through it completely;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	 and cut off the edge of the paper where the hairs emerge from those hairs, pull the thread above it all over the paper, and turn to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	 then make an incision in the part under the paper, beneath the hairs, all the way along the spatula from the large tear to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 Then draw the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and linen beneath the paper, then mark on the paper a shape like a thistle stalk, and it is necessary that the figure should be according to the size that you see the paper should be raised.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	 And if there is need for a large amount of paper according to how much the paper has been softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	 then make the whole stylus on the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large notch down to the small one;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	 and let it be one of the slits near the natural hairs at the thickness of a root, then push the onion into one of the two angles of the keyhole, then peel it entirely;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	 Then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle and fine linen thread, squeeze out the blood, and make the excess thread adhere to the two eyelids to any gluey substance, if you want to do this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	 and if not, if you have no treatment for it, then leave the stitch and the thread until three or four days.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	 then treat the wound without stitching with drying and constricting substances, for the paper relieves at the edge of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitch is rotten (as they say in the olden days), and this is not work done with fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	 and if another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And it is that you trace the paper with a figure like the fennel stalk, as we have stated, divided into three sections according to the form given here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then fold what is above the small areas equally according to the shape shown below:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	 And if you cannot hold the tongs and the thing is not even, take a needle with thread on it and pierce through the figure.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	 and put the other thread from the large notch, and the second thread from the small one, and arrange the threads equally between your fingers.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then flatten your hand equally and lift all the skin that you have signed, as we have stated, then sew together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and let it heal until it is healthy.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	 And if an abscess comes to your incision, appease it with cerote and similar soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	 Occasionally the hairs of the papier become converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	 If you must perform an incision, use what we have said about it.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 However, the stitching in one and the other is more artful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	 The treatment of dogs follows this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	 and it is that you convert the papier and fold it inside as I have said, and then make two dogs by art, and two fine strings as long as the papier and the width of the spatula.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	 and tie together the heads of the two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	 Then assemble one and the other gently on top of what is covered by the paper of oil, and hold the two cords of the two parts together.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 And leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is held will die and rot and fall off, as it decays through it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 If it takes too long, if necessary, heal it until it heals completely.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	 When the wound is healed, and when the paper is lifted, the hairs will not grow again;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 And this is the form of the two cords that you will make according to this figure and this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	 The work requires taking a thin needle and putting silk thread on it that is also thin.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	 Then gather the bones [shoulder] and bring them together gently, and may the thickness of the tendons be a palm's length.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	 then wind a thin thread of silk briefly around [the shoulder] and bind it with the thread.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	 then put the patient's head on a clean pillow.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	 and let the patient's head be removed from the sun so that the work is clear, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then insert the needle into the entire socket towards the root of the hair, and make it pierce through the paper quickly until you draw it over the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	 then pull out the hair up to the socket and insert into the socket the number of hairs, whether one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 Then stretch your hand until the hairs come out completely from all the chase on the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	 And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out, you will pull the chase beneath to the thread that you have prepared, until the chase comes out from the holes above and you see it through the eye of oil.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	 Then you will pull the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it for 2 or 3 days until the hair adheres in its place and the flesh grows up.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the hairs are small, accompany it with long natural hair and let it grow along with that which you leave, until it is stretched out and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	 When this disease called "alecrati" or porridge comes in the eye, it has two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly due to a wound or injury, or by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And the method of treatment is that you break the adhesion, separate the eyelids from it, put linen threads inside, and hold it until it heals.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 and it must not be that you use in its treatment of things that dry and constrict it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	 For if you do this, the disease becomes worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	 but the work of things softening, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 and the broth of water or milk and flaxseed should be cooked, and at once dip it in warm oil from dahiquil, wrap it in a linen cloth, and heal with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	 And the treasure of your cure is that you take care not to stitch it [the wound] in the same way as it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 and these things that we have said are not remedies for this disease except its proper alignment, so that it does not recur in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the chyle which comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This disease which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	 The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cauterizations and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	 and the procedure in this is that you take a needle with doubled thread, and pierce it into the flesh from the left eyelid to the right, so that the threads come out in two places of the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 then fold the skin over the entire needle and cover it with a wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	 And if the shape of the bone returns as it should, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	 If not, take the rasp and put it in the incision, turn the bone, and make two cuts along the inside of the bone;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	 and let the heads of the cuts at both angles of the incision you made be aligned, and let them form an angle such that when they are assembled, the shape will be as the shape of a letter which has the name "Greek";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	 then remove that cartilage, according to the thickness of its sides, underneath the bone, then join the two separated parts with a linen thread;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat it with the medicine we have mentioned for softening and poultices until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	 And if the disease comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, then you must make an incision in a plain area beneath the hairs of the paper (skin), and according to what was mentioned before;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	 Then cut between the two ribs of a tent, as I have said.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	 And the work should be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare instruments of all possible means to bring the figure back to its natural form.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 and the patients themselves, according to what work and instruments are required in multiple positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the sudden dislocation of the shoulder
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	 When this suture happens in the hands of men in such a way that the paper above is glued with the white part of oil and cannot move or perform its natural work, then you must push the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	 And hold it with forceps until you cut what is near the puncture point of the probe, which should not be too sharp nor too piercing, so that the patient does not suffer from a too-sharp probe piercing the oil.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	 And make your incision, which you peel apart that assembly, gently, so that the skin returns to its natural shape.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	 And heal all that assembly, and make once in the sharp oil salty, and raise from it sweet oil and bile.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	 Then put between the skin and the oil a tent of linen, and put on top of the oil wool soaked in abundance of egg.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And after three days use bile and other strong things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	 Know that the nail is according to two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	 the nail is either nerve-like and resembling hard stone, or another that is not nerve-like but resembles white frozen moisture, which when touched by iron and cooked with pliers cannot be moved.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 and both begin to approach the large root, and grow little by little until they cover the whole eye and all the light and the movement of oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	 And the method of incision is that the patient places their head on a healthy surface, then they open their eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	 and lift the paper in your hand, then take the nail with small tweezers, and stretch it above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	 Then take a needle, and put horse hair or cow hair, or strong thread on it.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	 and bend the tip of the needle a little and push it into the nail, and pierce through with the whole needle, and tie the nail with thread and hang it above, and shave all the hair on the side of the nail that follows the curve and the silk to the hair up to the root, then chop the remaining in the root of the finger at the very tip of the spatula and small force, and leave the natural flesh or nail so that by incision the body does not produce tears as usual.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	 and sometimes the nails grow at the edge only, and with thread, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 Then scrape all the putty-like substance of this kind from the wound:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	 And ensure that the spatumile does not touch the skin flap and tear it, and that the puncture is not made.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And after incising, pour oil a little piece of crushed silk and make a collirium from litarge, and leave it until the next day.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat those that need it until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	 And if the nail is not nerve-ridden, and you cannot push the needle, and the unguis cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is treated with medicine.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And as I told in the division, if it grows as I have described and you see it covered with oil from the patient, take a small amount of the spatumile as shown here:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And the nail above (should be) scraped gently, and if you see that it doesn't diminish at all and reason follows, then distill from your mouth into the collyrium oil made of litargyre and red collyrium powder, and stop the oil until the next day.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 Then repeat the other work according to this same work, until it is completely opened.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing prevents you in the oil, as in the treatment of an abscess, first milk it, and heal the abscess hot until it is healed, then repeat the procedure as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	 And if the appearance of the flesh from the sore harms the oil greatly, stop it at the edge, and cut off a part and not all, so that tears do not come.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 Then distill in the red collyrium oil made of litargyre.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Of the flesh which grows upon the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	 In some men, red pus sometimes arises, covering the eyelid and pressing on top of paper and turning towards the tear duct, appearing like a rosebud.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	 And the operations are such that the patients put their head on the healthy side, then they cut open the eyes, and hold all that skin suitable for this purpose firmly with strength.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	 Then cut the first piece of flesh and go cutting to the end with the razor until the end, and be careful not to pierce the oil at the operation.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	 And make the incision with a spathule, as we have said in the incision of the nail and the small forces of which one removes the scab, according to the shape after this chapter it demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	 And when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, use oil of cedar pulverized or you distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and put over the oil fleece with egg white, to ensure that it heals without pus.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	 And if there remains something, and the wound is shallow, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave the oil and treat the abscess with things soothing an abscess.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 Then return to your work when it is healthy, and thus do as charms are anointed with oil in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	 But nevertheless, you must lighten the care of each weak oil by the natural way.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	 and of the accidental way, in work with iron.
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 And do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is strong enough for this work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Should be red veins that are covered on the oil, and they drain their work and weaken the oil day and night.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	 Therefore, first you should look to see if the oil, in which the stone is, is hollow, and has no other illness except the stone.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	 Then tie the neck thus:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 instruct the patient to place his head in a loop, then tie those bands all around evenly according to his wisdom, and may the loops be subtle and double as shown here:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two points in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	 then tie those bands tightly and squeeze out the blood hour by hour until you see those loops move away from the oil;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	 and ensure that you do not prick the oil with the tips of the spatulas, and perform this task at noon in the sun, and be very warm in your work so that the loops do not break.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 and when you have done this, if you can distill green and red oil of collyrium to treat those that remain stubborn with the scab.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if you cannot collect all of it in that hour, apply a plaster on the oil of soothing things to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is alleviated and is secure from abscess, then continue as before until it heals;
et c’est li forme des forces:	 And this is the form of the cautery (procedure):
de la fistule de l’oil	From the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	 The surgeon is called "arissati" (inciser):
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 When you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick in it that you make an incision over the abscess where it should die, and drain out all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	 And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, if it requires all the instruments as described here;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 And it is called "sharp head", and it should be made from iron pointed like a chisel as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	 And place the iron on the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little so that you know that the corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And do this once, then restore the bone with medicine extractors.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 If the joint is fused and pus appears, and the corpse of the bowel remains fused for 40 days without renewal or abscessing, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	 If there is no other remedy than to return the fistula to the pierced navels as follows:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 and you make an incision in the bone for the second time with iron, and with hot medicines, and when it is exposed, take the iron drill according to this form, and let the points of the iron be at three angles, and the shaft should be tapered up to the head as you can see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	 then place it on the bone at the junction of the rim, and move your hand away from the oil hole, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the vein if he holds his hand on his navel.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	 and afterwards restore the place with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when the flesh hardens and strengthens the joint, the matter goes to the navel.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 It is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the dislocation
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	 When all the eyes (pupils) are opened wide in every direction and there is no obstruction or dimming of the sight, you must tie down the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	 Then apply medicine to the healthy eye, or use tweezers with iron to aid in sucking, then place oil made from acacia, aloe, incense and saracocolla on it, then hold the oil and pour it onto bandages and cloths.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	 The manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one four times, then put one on top of the other according to the amount needed.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	 then hold it in place with a hard bandage and repeat the use of tweezers for suction without iron.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	 Then remove the cysts and leave the oil constrained for a day and night, and if they have healed together, then you must stretch it greatly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	 Then remove the ligament the next day and night, and if you see the oil healing, that is good;
se ce non;	 if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 if it is not, then repeat the plaster and dressings and ligament and cysts until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The double rupture of the ruptured membrane.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	 When dislocations occur in the inflamed cloth, then open it, and force out the paper as if with grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	 Therefore, if you see it covered, the procedure is such that you push an awl into the root of the affected part all the way up to the opposite side, then push another awl or one with a doubled thread from the edge of the abscess.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	 And make it pierce, let the first needle follow the position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	 then pull through the thread and tie a part of the vein around it tightly, then draw out the needle and put soft oiled woolen yarn on top of it abundantly.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	 and leave it until the thread sticks to the vein, then heal the oil with comforting things until the wound heals.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 and sometimes the wound is held closed by the vein on each side of a circle of fabric until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	 And if the eyes appear large, pierce them with a fine spatula that comes from the oil and correct the moisture abscess and drain the eyes, and put in something immediately.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then draw [the shoulder] out until it is in its socket again.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bowl of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	 This disease called "alcunnati" is not far from the oil, it resembles an inflamed eye socket and is not an inflamed eye;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	 and the method of treating it is to make the patient sit on a stool facing the affected side, then take the head between your hands from both sides and move it until you see the bone come up to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	 then insert a probe, do not drain the pus and open the light [the wound], let the patient see what is there as he is accustomed.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 and if it does not drain below [the probe], know that it is inflamed, and if the dislocation of the bone is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	 Make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and poke through the cornea-like cloth into the eye socket with the cornea and bone, as long as it bores through.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when it is extracted, distill cold sharp oil mixed with honey or hot water with fenugreek, or honey, into it; then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	 We have the appearances of eyes in division, and those that must be pierced;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 if they are healthy.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	 The patient should be seated between your hands with crossed legs, away from the light and the sun, and hold the oil clean and squeeze it very tightly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	 Then place the oil paper on your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or on your right hand if the eyes are on the right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	 Then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	 then place the point of the instrument under the crown through the thickness of a finger in that oil-filled sac at the lower part of the eyelid, then push the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and hold your hand steady until it pierces into the oil sac, and feel that almagda enters the empty space.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	 and it is necessary that the measurement of the way almagda be at the full length of the space which is from the eyelash to the end of the eyebrow.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	 And it is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 You will see the bone on this paper through the brightness of the horned parchment, and then place the instrument up to it or where it is sharp, and press afterwards.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If the wound begins to drain now, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in its oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	 After a short rest, and if the sharp point rises on the second vein, press with the instrument, and when it is fully inserted and does not rise further, gently stretch it around by turning your hand bit by bit.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 Then replace the sharp point with a little gemmy silk, and cut away that oil from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then pour in the oil of lavender or moistened cloth soaked in rose oil and abundant egg, and bind it with the oil of lard.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, place a thin layer of beaten egg white on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard hairs, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	 Therefore pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make it delicate, then gently push it in as we said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	 And upon completion of the work, the patient sleeps on his back in a dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	 Rest from all movements, take light foods, do not move your head either to the right or left, and bind him according to his position for three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	 Then unbind him in the same dark house, test his vision, show him some things, and then bind him again for seven more days.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And it is not necessary to do this during the course of the treatment or after the incision now, but you should reduce this, because the pain increases quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	 If an abscess comes up, unbind the oil before the seventh day, and direct that which eases the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 And when it is calmed down, loosen the eye and place it on its side to cover for any day, and stay always in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	 Then little by little, go out of the house and turn into your condition;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	 And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in our land they do almagda perciet, so that it drips water, but I have never seen anyone doing it in our land, nor have I ever heard of it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	 And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them will see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	 And they are of arsenic properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these should be of the same subtlety, and the rear in four angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh near the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	 Sometimes charms or diverse-looking scorptions are born, from which there are some that seem like real scorpions with many legs;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 If there are any of these or if the charm has changed to such a color and if the charm is soft in bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	 Therefore, for those charms that are soft and not hardened, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	 Open their nostrils, and pour the onion juice onto those charms, and drive them out strongly.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Then grasp that which you can support with a thin and sharp spatula on one side, until you know that the charm is completely destroyed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	 And if anything remains that cannot be covered, open it completely with all sharp and subtle instruments, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	 and if the abscess is not healed and an arrow remains, seek help as necessary.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 and if it is a malicious abscess, act quickly and burn until the pus is drained and all the charred matter is removed, then apply cool oil or vinegar and water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 If there is no healing and moisture comes up to the mouth, know that it is healthy.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	 and if moisture does not come out as necessary, know that there is pus in the bone above, so instruments do not come to cut it.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	 Then you should put in some yarn, about an inch thick, and it should be tied by our hands, with space between each knot no less.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	 and place the patient's head in yarn through its neck as far as it can go, and pull while smelling until it comes out of the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	 and children in schools often do this, and it is an easy thing for someone who wants to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 then hold the head coming through the neck with one hand and the other head coming from the mouth with the other hand, and let one after the other pass by our hands that are tied together by yarn.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	 Do this until you know that the knots have rotted the flesh, then pull the yarn, squeeze out the blood, wet the yarn in Egyptian ointment and put it back into the neck again as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	 Make it last for three days or more, until the burns consume all that remains of flesh.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	 And then place or insert a plug of yew wood for some days until it is drained, and if there is need for drying medicine, use it.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 And this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, where oil and medicines are distilled.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	 And it is made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a plug, and lead it likewise.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	 And if you wish, make a closed plug, and let the instrument be hollow for purging the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	 Many times, in the head of the nose, there arises a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large over time until it can be seen with the eye.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	 And for this reason, you must cut it at the beginning and burn all of it, then place the hot cautery or burning medicine on its place.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	 And if you delay cutting it when it is large, beware if it is hard, of such color, poor sensitivity.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	 Do not touch it with iron as it is an inflamed abscess, for when you cut it even once, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 If the abscess is soft and of such color, you can cut it all, empty the patient and cut it cautiously without fear, then treat the place with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 When solutions come continuously into one of these work cartilages, it helps little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	 Therefore, when such an occurrence happens to anyone, one should look if the wound is fresh with all its blood.
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then align the two lips together in a stitch, then heal it until it heals completely.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	 If the lips are separated on both sides, then you must cauter all their parts until they heal, then align the two lips together in a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood powder and incense powder.
