Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	 And if you find or skin rot, it is not on the bone, bind the entire rotten part and throw away pus, then cure it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	 And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cauterization, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie it with a thread if you find it dislocated.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	 And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light.
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And you put on this powder that causes it to heal as soon as the air touches it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	 The method of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	 Take incense, some of it;
sanc de dragon II parties;	 The blood of a dragon, two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	 Live coal in three parts, and apply the fine powder to the wound, and press it firmly, until it purges well and unites with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	 And then tie it up well, and let it heal on its own if it does not swell.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 for medicine should not be applied until the wound is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes they do this with only chalk, when there is no incense nor dragon's blood, but the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	 And if the burn has opened the wound, by all means do not apply this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	 But apply certain digestive herbs or barley flour made with water and honey until it stops weeping.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	 If a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, pull it apart gently using delicate forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And I will tell you afterwards about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound    (literal translation)
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one in the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.   (literal translation)
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	 If it is the nerves, there is no other instrument but to leave them alone and not put anything binding, because it harms the nerves and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	 and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 But the medicine should be warm, like water boiled in sweet oil and rosewater, and also boiled water moistened with other similar stones, and instantly moist.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, bind it with strips, then let it heal until it becomes healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	 And if the wounds are deep and swollen and full of pus, pierce or deeper.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	 And if the artery is cut, bleeding occurs, stop it, tie it, and cauterize as necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	 And if the spinal cord of the neck is cut or pierced, and it is guided, keep it, so that the meat goes along with it, then tie the wound above the neck of the neck, and do not touch the throat but return it to its natural position.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then straighten it gradually and leave it for some days, then heal it with disinfected onions until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	 And if the wound presses against the bone, pierce it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	 And if there are fragments of bone, pull them all out if possible, and those that cannot be pulled out, leave it until the wound heals and disinfects and aligns the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on it as I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is bone in the wound and a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	 If it is a spear or knife wound and the wound gapes, check if the patient exhales air from the wound.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	 Then know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	 If it is not deep, and the wound is still fresh with blood, do not immediately apply powder or tie it up for the blood to clot and return to the heart, take care of the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	 But apply atracitive ointment and tie it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	 And if you don't have ointment, place a piece of old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture and let the patient sleep on the wound for 3 or 4 days or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	 If it does not come spasm or bad tremors of heart nor strangeness of aliens;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 And when you see the good dispositions, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Treat then with cautery and other remedies, as long as it is sound;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	 And if it cannot heal, open it up, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	 If the treatment is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or deeper, or on the back, treat that which is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	 if it is large, sew it up.
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	 if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone and has pieces in it, open the wound and pull out the fragments if they are dislodged;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	 And if they are not drained, let the wound fester, align the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 For other wounds on various members, the judgments are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The displacement of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	 The ruptures in the belly can be large, medium-sized, or small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	 From a large wound, one time the intestines may protrude, or the nerves of the intestines, due to which the insertion of fingers;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	 And the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worth less than a large one, because when the intestines are put back in, they are put in piece by piece if not done all at once.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	 because the intestines swell quickly when they feel cold, so they are put back more often, and therefore the smaller wounds are worse than the large ones, because the intestines must be reset to their place more frequently than others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	 And know that the hernia of the belly is according to four kinds:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	 The two common stitchings occur in the hernia of the belly, and the stitches for other wounds on the body and the other specific stitches are common for other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 And each of them is more suitable with the stitching of the belly, and I will say one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	 When the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines has protruded, and there is little to return, this is suitable for one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are inflated due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	 And when it is cold, heat it in this way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 Moisten a sponge or a piece of linen in warm water only, or cook it in warm quince and cypress and pepper, and rub the intestines until the inflammation is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And at times, this wine constricting is made, and it is to be moved like sulfur for inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	 And when you see the inflammation spreading, if the intestines are cooked with too much or too little water or poor quality, for this reason the entry is blocked to almost nothing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	 And if it cannot enter, make a small wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	 And the first remedy is boiled leek, which one should not cut excessively or it will lose its effect.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	 and this is the instrument to split (it):
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 cut through lengthwise but not too deep, and look at its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines fall out, you should put them back in their natural place in their proper position, if you have the ability, because it is important to do so.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	 When the wound is wide and located in the lower part of the abdomen, you must make the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	 If the wound is in one of the two parts below the abdomen, you must make sure that the affected part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 And thus it is necessary to apply what I say on large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	 On small wounds, apply what is provided to you, then take pitying hands that cover the entire wound with their hand and press the lips together.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	 and this is the common way of suturing, and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the width of the wound, then leave from the edge of the wound a space, and insert a needle where it has strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	 and pierce the two bones of the skin with the two bones of the sinew, which is under the skin from that part, until you have pierced it through, and join the two heads of the sinew together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	 then draw the thread through both parts of the needle, then join the two bones of the wound together in order, and then leave a space, and insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	 Then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing so according to what is needed for the needles, until all the wound is held in place.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	 And let the needles be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick; for thin needles pierce through all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	 because they must be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	 And it is not good to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, so that they do not pierce and open up the wound before the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	 Then tie the heads of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put weights or cloths on the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	 And this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it pierces an awl or two there.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	 The second type of stitching is common, and that you assemble the two bones of the skin and the two bones of the flesh together with a single needle having a medium thick thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	 and when you have pierced all the bones four together, then withdraw the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that garments are sewn.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	 and put space between each stitch of a fingertip's thickness.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 This stitching is for a man, and I sewed a wound that a knight had in the belly, which was stabbed with a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and it was the intestines that were two palms deep inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestine before it had been XXIV hours [outside], and the wound was sewn up for 15 days, and it healed, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	 And they had judged him to be dying, but it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	 and I did not treat him with salve because I was in a place where none was found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 and I placed cotton over the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	 Now I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing [or: stitching]:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	 take the needle and thrust it from outside to inside the part.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	 when it has penetrated the core straight through, then take hold of the end of the thread or stitch where you inserted the needle, and pierce it from the inside to outside at another spot.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 The meaning of this sentence is that the understanding of this stitch is that you sew it as furriers sew pelts, and that you leave an opening once from one side, then return it from the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	 The second manner of stitching, which Galen calls specifically, is when two parts are assembled naturally and one edge of the opening is applied to the other edge in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	 Insert a needle or point the mirror close by, and make it pierce only that place, and leave the two edges of the opening.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	 then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside to that within, through the two edges of the opening.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	 Then pierce one and the other of the outer part right up to the inside, in two shoulders at the opposite sides.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 And this is the usual way of suturing and the most common method.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	 Galen said this word, and no one can deny it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	 And one needle should be inserted from one side, and the other from the other, as those who sew leather do.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Know that when the wound is in the belly, the suturing is more painful than other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	 The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	 And when you find the fresh wound filled with blood, as soon as the arrow has moved it, then put in again the intestines and the flesh.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	 Then put on a healing charcoal powder and if the arrow has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	 And stitch the flesh, and bind the suture and the mirror.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then treat the wound as the others do, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 If you have no medicine, put on old cotton immediately when it begins to ooze pus, and stir it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	 For you do not need other medicines in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	 And if you doubt that the wound spreads to the main members, then it is necessary for you to apply light linen dipped in warm oil or rose oil around the injuries and under the joints.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	 And if there is pain or swelling in the belly and it often happens, then clisterize with black wine and particularly when the corruption reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 And pierce it through, know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine known as "jeun" cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is because of the inflammation of the veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	 And if the hernia jumps out of the wound, put it back in place as with the intestine, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	 And if it is old and has turned black or green, you must tie the part that is black, so that blood flow does not come from it, because there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 Then catch what is between the ligament, and hang the two heads hanging from the part below the wound so as to straighten the extraction when the sinews fall out, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the eyeball
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	 If the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I have seen that a man was pierced or stabbed in the abdomen with a spear.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	 and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became abscessed and turned into a fistula, and in this there were discharges and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 I gave it treatment according to what I knew, and did not stop subsiding until it was healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	 And when I see it sutured (stitched), I doubt if the patient has something wrong in his stomach.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	 and he had no sickness, but remained in better conditions, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	 and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied (sutured) in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	 take large forceps with big handles, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the forceps have opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches its mouth over.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	 and then you strike its head, holding it so that it cannot be disengaged (loosened), and then put another forceps following in the same manner until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	 And dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	 If the head becomes inflamed in the intestine and brings no harm to the patient, it can be tied with a fine thread made from the intestine of an animal in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	 take the head of this intestinal thread that is finely sharpened, then tie it to the head of a fine linen thread twisted, then put the thread in the needle and sew up the intestine, and pull it out through an incision.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	 and this method of sewing inflammation has no force unless according to the way of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no trick or health, but only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it heals and forms a cavity, is universally called "fistula", and the same when it is closed and becomes hollow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	 And fistula is according to nature a hard and white nodulation, where no pain is felt, and it is as hollow as the feather of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	 sometimes clear and at other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	 sometimes small, and at other times large.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	 and I have spoken about it in the section on wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, this is foreign only by one of the NINE reasons:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	 meaning, by the scarcity of blood or body.
ou por sa malice;	 or by its corruption;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	 or because there is hard flesh within, and above the lips, that does not allow new flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	 There is too much pus.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	 The joint is dislocated, and the substance is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	 or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	 because corruption is a kind of plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	 because in the area, digestion is slow, health takes time to recover, and it runs away by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	 there are veins or bones.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 I have already shown all these causes, signs, and remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it is necessary that I tell you the treatment for fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	 Fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	 because there are fistulas that come from the large veins, arteries, nerves, or in the groin, intestines, bladder, one of the ribs, spine on the back, or any joint of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 And if it comes to the property of the main member and its similar joints.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	 All such fistulas are of severe healing, and there is no remedy for them except labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	 And if there is any fistula that does not come out until the level I have said and you are confident of its cure, and you recognize it, take a tent of goose or iron, if the fistula is straight, apply it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	 And if the fistula is crooked, search for a thin tent of lead, because lead bends with curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	 And if the fistula is pierced in many places and you cannot search for it with tents, then cleanse one of the openings, because moisture quickly moves from one opening to another, and purify it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	 Then carefully feel with your power if there is bone or nerve and whether it is hardened, and ask the patient in detail about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	 and when you know the truth about its location and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery or vein, or in any of the locations I have mentioned, then cut according to what I said, and remove the fracture and corrupt tissue that is inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	 and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well opened straight through, you must cut deeply, as far as you can, then put wet bandages soaked in a strong medicine into it, and push them up to the tip of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous material that remains inside.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then put on oil-soaked linen cloths until it heals;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And if it doesn't heal by that, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the wound, strike it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	 If neither vein nor nerve affects or major limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove it until all corruption is removed, then apply oil-soaked linen cloths until it heals;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	 And if it doesn't heal and the condition worsens as before, know that you are not going to the font (fountain);
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	 If you expose it and dig as deep as you can, and remove all corruption, then reset the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 And if it remains thus sound, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	 If it is not like that, know that the corruption is too advanced, you will not be able to achieve it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	 if there is no other remedy than waiting for nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	 and if there is only a little bone corrupted, and you can draw it with the pliers, take out the one that seems appropriate for that, and if there are many bones, draw them all, do not leave any of them.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 and if the moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, strike the moisture and the flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something repellent corruption on the wound, and leave it until the flesh grows around the bones, and then they will more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	 And if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, only remove the corruption until all the blackness has disappeared, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	 If there is a large part of corruption and it reaches to the bone marrow;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	 it must be cut and covered up to the corruption, and then heal until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 I will tell you about a fistula that happened in the thigh of a man, take this as an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	 A young man about 30 years old had pain in his leg due to an internal cause causing matter to come to the leg, and there was a large abscess that could not be opened.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	 However, due to their foolishness, they overburdened the abscesses too much, and in doing so, they corrupted a great deal of matter, which became a fistula, and much pus emerged that all were wet with moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	 and many patients put themselves under treatment for about two years, without any wise man in the art of hands, until I was summoned to them, and saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and what ran through the pus at great expense.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 And the young man's body became red, and had a yellow tint.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I inserted a tent in one of the wounds, and then I searched for all the wounds, and found that some came towards each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	 Then I hurried and made an incision in one of the sores until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot reached the bone within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	 I appeared to me as if the bone was rotten, and I thought there was no other corruption, except that which I left.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	 and began to apply balms of sodium to the wound for a long time, but could not heal it.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	 and then I recommenced, and exposed the bone as before, and found that the corruption was continuous in the bone, and I removed it, and then left it, and thought about healing the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	 but I could not heal more than I wrapped around a palm of the bone, and then let it be completely exposed, and applied balms to it.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 and it healed and was healed quickly, and there was no need to resume the work except due to the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and due to the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation (procedure), it often bleeds profusely, but it became completely healthy, and a hard cyst grew in the bone's place, and it was well-positioned and had no harm or disadvantage in any way, neither in its appearance nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	 And if the bone is broken at any place in the body, it must be thus set:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	 Take thread, and hold the tip of the broken bone open, and command anyone to stretch it upward;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	 and put another thicker thread of flax over the first thread, tie it above the flesh that is stripped from the bone, stretch it out to pull the corrupted flesh below, exposing the healthy flesh where you wish it to be, so that the bone does not pierce the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	 and put a splint or plaster under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 It must be held until it can be seen and felt that the corruption has subsided, and it should be held again at other times.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	 And if the bone is corrupt and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, you should uncover the flesh entirely.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	 Then put the iron on it, and then soak one part of the corruption from the other end, and the soaked area should be the length of the corruption as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	 and if the corruption is at a joint, you should break the corrupt joint, and you should soak the bone on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	 and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy but to break it.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	 and if the corruption is at the base of the hand or foot, it is a very difficult thing, but nevertheless you must investigate this corruption to see how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	 And clean it in all ways as you can, but let neither the vein nor the nerve hinder you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	 And know that the saws and files for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	 And therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each type of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	 And know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to your knowledge of this art and the testimony of the forms of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 If you consider the instrument that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	 The shoulder may dislocate either from within or from outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	 and when you have administered that corrosive cure through medicine, and it does not help, then it is necessary to cover the affected limb up to the point where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient suffers from death or greater evil due to the defect of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	 And the signs are that the limbs become black, as if they have been burnt by fire, and afterwards the blackness spreads from member to member, and it takes over the entire body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 If it is haste by the sting of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and a viper and others, if the corrosion is at the top of the neck, then strike it, but do not allow it to come up as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	 And if it comes up to the hand, then strike at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	 And if it reaches the forearm, then strike at the elbow.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	 And if it pierces through [the flesh], it is death, and there is no help but in the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	 And thus do as when the corruption comes or the putrefaction:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	 If it comes at the first joint, then strike after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	 and if it comes on the foot, then strike the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	 and if it rises in the leg, then strike at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	 and if it comes above the knee, then the patient has no other remedy but to die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	 The manner of striking or healing the limb is that you bind it above and below, stretch a minister on one of the tendons below, and another minister on the other tendon above, and you compress the flesh between the two tendons with a spatula wide enough to expose the bone.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 Then strike or heal, and place linen cloth on both sides so that the blow does not touch healthy flesh, causing the patient other injury and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	 And if bleeding comes when you work, then cauterize the area immediately, or apply some powders to restrict it.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the limb with a tight bandage and cure it until it heals.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	 and I will tell you what happened at the house of the peasant:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	 a farmer had a burn that looked like it was scorched by fire, and the corruption first appeared in his foot of the peasant, until it spread over the entire foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	 and when the farmer saw the corruption, he covered his foot with copper and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	 A long time later, the corruption returned to his hand, and he came to me. I gave him remedies after purifying the body, but the corruption could not be stopped.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	 And he orders me to crush the hand, and I promise that I have no hope of repelling the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	 Furthermore, he also doubts if I would cut off his hand, as the vitality of the man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	 And he gave up all hope and returned to his land, and decided to cut off his own hand, and it healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 I have told this story only because such is sometimes done if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	 Sometimes an abscess occurs in the shinbone and lasts so long that it causes a large swelling of the leg;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	 Then they run and pierce it, causing the leg to jump, and the bones appear visible, like a knight;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	 And the skin that is above is as thin as unspun cloth, and it will not penetrate to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such disease is called "sores", and is not called "fistulas".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	 but if it is so long that it comes to the bone in depth, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	 and the skin is such that you can cut all around it, and equally when it is thin, as cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 and does not spread due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	 And if you have reason to believe that the skin is spreading and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with fat, then treat it with clysters in this way:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	 Look if the breasts are large, and the belly that is in it has a foul smell, then clisterize with Egyptian medicine which is made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	 Take asafetida, oil, and litharge equally, cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	 and then take from this according to your need, make it into water and honey, and clisterize the breast, and press the abscess.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	 leave the medicine in for two hours, then strain it.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	 do this many times until the breast is purified and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	 and sometimes clisterize with water of ashes when this medicine is not present, and take vine ash, pour water over it, let it cool, and then clisterize with it until you know that the breast has been purified.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	 If the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then clisterize with water and honey or have a little powdered lead;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	 or you clisterize with honey and sweet wine, as the honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the blood less viscous.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	 and when you have done this and you are confident that the breasts are well cleaned, then you clisterize with what causes milk to grow in them, and take an emplastrum, make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	 or you clisterize with certain medicines and ointments, as I have said the properties for treating wounds.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	 And if the abscess in the breast is small and the cannula of the cupping glass cannot enter, widen it a little with a knife, and put on a tent of the Egyptian ointment or ointment of basilicon until it is widened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the wound is too large, leave it only enough room so that the cupping glass or cannula can enter, and if there is a pus-filled boil above it, bring it down or lower it slightly.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	 For when the boil is ripe, do not let any flesh grow into it;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	 And if you cannot cover the breast as desired, arrange it in such a way that the boil moves to its lowest position, because when the boil is ripe, do not let any flesh grow into it and if you cannot cover the breast as desired.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	 The bow moves gently forward, and do not let go of anything from the bow.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	 Take medicines that consolidate and place them on the wound, then stretch it over a linen cloth that covers the entire wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	 Then push the force against the wound in the chest, slightly larger than the first one, then anoint it gently with oil on another cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it over the wound of the chest to straighten the bow, but do not remove the large cloth except after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	 And the one on the wound of the chest, often removes it to straighten the bow, and knows what will come out from the bow, whether it is poison or pus or digestible or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	 And beware if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been administered in this manner and you see the pus rising, know that the breast has turned sour, and approach the healthy.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 Then loosen it in the morning or at midday, and when you dislocate the wound, change another linen cloth and renew the salve.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	If the breasts overflow with undigested matter for many days, know that the breasts do not swell.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle venomous worms come after a long time, do not despair of health, for it approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	 For there are men whose wounds heal too slowly in linens, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	 And if it swells improperly from the breast after many days, know that the breast will not turn sour.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	 And if the breast takes too long to heal and is far away, join drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in effect, such as diaphytum, for there is great use of vitriol, and it is the final medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	 Take a definition of diaphytic, make it with rose oil, and mix equal parts of old wine in its substance.
puis le confit et en use;	 then apply and use it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	 and do the same more cooked and thickened when the diaphytic ointment is not present. Or take myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them into powder and sprinkle it on the honey while it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	 and then dab it on the cloth and place it on the breast. Sometimes an astrologer long is administered to it, and roots of celestial lily, which is like flour and cinnamon.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	 and use simple herbs or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	 grind them, make powder, and sprinkle it on the honey that I said, and apply.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	 And if the limb is long and not treated by this remedy, then know that corruption has fully set in, and it causes pressure on the bone or hardening of the tendons.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 If the wound is treated with the fire cautery as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail bed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 Panearice is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or by chance in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	 And when it is neglected and no care is taken, the abscess swells and corrupts and runs towards the root of the nail, and in some cases, it may corrupt the entire nail.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 The corruption reaches the bone, causing a strong-smelling pain, and the toes become swollen and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, and cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	 The cauteries are very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is intact.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	 and if the nail is below the skin and begins to point and swell, you must put oil beneath the nail so that it does not pierce the skin, and push it upwards, strike the swollen part gently but finely, and place hot and corrosive medicines on top to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then cure it with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	 And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike and draw it out, because as much as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if you see the tooth decay, strike it with a drill as mentioned before, then heal it until it heals.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	 And if it is wounded and pierced, and causes great pain, then you must first cleanse it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	 Then cut the nail with a sharp spatula perpendicularly across, and make sure that the cutting does not reach the skin beneath the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 and if it happens, place something on top of it to alleviate.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the hand gradually subsides.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 One must straighten the fingers that are born in some people by chance, and they are all flesh, and sometimes there is skin or bone there, and occasionally there is a nail; and none of these grow from the root of a joint, or their growth is in one of our palms.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	 The one who is born in any part of the body does not move, and the one who is born at the joint of the finger, by chance moves.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	 The cutting of the fleshy one should be easy in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 Cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	 The one who is born in the root of the joint should be treated carefully:
si te tien dou coper.	 cover it up.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who is born or should be in the last nail, you must cut the flesh roundly up to the bone first, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and then treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together in the fingers also come together by birth, or by injury, or by fire burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	 If it is necessary to cut the suture, it should be reattached according to their natural shapes;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	 then place a piece of linen or cloth soaked in rose oil between them so they do not fuse together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 or you may put between two thin boards until the wound is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Similarly, if it comes to either of its sides with the palm, you strike the joint as necessary.
des vils	 of peasants
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	 These are swellings large and full of melancholic humors that come in many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 And it happens more often in legs of those who walk or work or carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purge of bile at times, and then the healthy from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The treatment of iron is according to two methods: [This sentence is not a complete statement and does not translate literally. It seems to mean that there are two ways to treat iron, but without more context it's difficult to provide an accurate translation.]
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 One is to strike them [the iron objects], and the black blood is drawn out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 And another way is that you open a vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 The cutting is as follows according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 First, the lower leg is raised with strong hot water until the flesh becomes thin, then hold the patient's leg from above the calf to below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	 then cut the vein in one of the three places (I, II, or III) with a large incision, then separate and draw out black blood to your hand from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's condition can tolerate.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	 and then tie it up, and instruct the patient to bind himself with meat broth colored black;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 And resume the evacuation and healing when veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	 The application of the leeches is as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	 Reheat the patient's leg if there is much hair, then place it in warm water, and rub the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	 If there is no warm water, heat it over the fire, and then press it against the vein along the thigh or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	 Then, with the blade, cut the skin to the edge, and peel off the vein from both sides, as much as you can feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	 When it becomes red and black, and when it comes through the skin like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	 Then push the bone back inside, until it is raised from the skin, and then cut it at the edge lightly, then press it in another place three inches away.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	 Then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then rinse with warm water, as you have done before, and make an incision at another location, as you did previously.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	 Make another incision, or more if necessary, then rinse, and make it at the base of the foot, then draw it out and rinse until the second incision.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	 Then extract it bit by bit until it all comes out, then seal it up.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	 And if you cannot pull it out and lift it, push an awl through the entire length, tie it and draw, then push it beneath the skin, and turn your hand from one side to another until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	 And guard that it does not swell, for if it swells, it cannot be drawn nor lifted, and it is harmful to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	 And when you have treated everything, place on the wound a linen cloth dampened with vinegar and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and heal it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	 And if the wound is contracted, twisted and rolled together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must make an incision, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 and draw it out as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The shape of the iron used to pierce the vein should be curved and not cut, but rather open the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 and is of large curvature, because if it is thin, it would pierce the vein; but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein is opened in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on dry ground without moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 And possibly it may be found in other places than the legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes from under the skin, as it comes inside the body like a snake, opening up between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg and then the joint changes and the vein starts to forcefully appear, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the head is opened, you must wrap around a piece of wood from 1.5 inches to 2.5 inches and sew it up, and leave the wood on the leg, and whenever there is leakage, you should re-wrap and sew it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 and if it is too long, you must cut a part of it, wrap the remaining part, but do not cover the root, until it is completely expelled.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 If you cut [it], it returns to the flesh, causes an abscess and pus or a bad disease at that place.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 Therefore, it is necessary that it should be treated little by little until the neck [or head], and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 And sometimes this vein, when it is treated for five or ten inches, a man came to me who had it come out from ten inches, and when you cut [it], it swells up like a balloon or a bladder, and pierces through to the bottom, so that everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 And empty the matter that is inside, and bring medicine against pus to the place for several days, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 And sometimes at this vein, many tears flow, and especially when it opens in the joint of the arm or leg, causing much harm, from which blood flows repeatedly.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 Then do as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land because it often occurs in cattle, and is a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body expanding and shrinking, and causing pain from one limb to another wherever it moves or jumps.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 and is engendered by the putrefaction of some bodily fluids, like worms, snakes, lizards, or roundworms in the abdomen.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 And there is doubt about its nature, for when it travels through the body, it ascends to the head and reaches the eye, by chance entering and destroying the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you wish to cure and draw it, one cannot force it out except when it is moving:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 Therefore, you must lie the limb above and below with a strong ligament tightly, then hit it upwards and draw it out forcefully, and if it turns inside towards the flesh and you cannot grasp it, you must cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 And the greatest damage that it does is that it causes an eye infection, as we have said.
