et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 And if you see it approaching or close to the eye, hold a ring beneath it, then hit upwards and draw it out forcefully.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 And it is necessary to use the patient with purification of the body with soluble medicines for expelling bad humors, and boil food that is spoiled and rotten.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 Of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This disease is called "vakirir" on our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from one limb to another;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 And I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was summoned to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm to me, and I saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 And then, it appeared to climb like a worm into the shoulder, very quickly, as fast as living silver when it cuts from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 The pain spread from that place and pierced into the shoulder, then shortly afterwards ran through the entire body until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then she told me that it kept turning around the body, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from one member to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 However, I wanted many times that the pain moved from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and that's why that constrained breathlessness appeared.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 And it does not appear in accordance with this reasoning to those who are ill and have moist bodies and veins closed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, you must lay it above and below quickly, and then press on top so that the constricted breathlessness returns to its place.
et cauterize le leu;	 Cauterize the place.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure that which expels the breathlessness, such as fetic pills and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their shapes and according to the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The diversities among them is such that there are some who have large points, small, sharp and soldered.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 and of those which have angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those where there are fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 and that which falls in any member falls according to two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 or in a primary member, like the brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidney, intestines, stomach, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it falls therefore in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 you should be careful with the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 And if this bad symptom is not evident to you, and the arrow is not fully inserted, draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 And when the skull symptom occurs with an arrow striking the bone, and a swelling appears on top of the skull, it is accompanied by symptoms such as scotoma (blindness in part of the visual field), pain in the head, throbbing and twisting, reddening around the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 And by chance, without force from the nostrils, or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 and by chance, it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 and jumps from the wound white matter resembling pus, and also as boiling water;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 and if this sign appears, hold back from treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not in;
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 The sign of an arrow when it falls or pierces the heart are that it is close to the left nipple and feels like it has been driven into a hard object, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 And by chance, the arrow becomes silent like pus, and black blood comes out, and coldness and sweat come, and fainting;
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The patient understands death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that never pierces the flesh is when bubbles rise from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, sighs loudly and seeks fresh air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 If the arrow falls under the bed, it should be removed from the flanks;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 and draw a long line and cause great pain and suffering.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And all the limbs of the shoulders move. (in the shoulders, all the limbs are moving)
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If an arrow falls into the stomach, possibly something from indigested meat may escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If an arrow falls into the belly and nothing escapes from the intestines through the wound, there is no hope in the treatment or removal of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 If an arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and spills, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 Know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, as the hand, arm, throat, shoulder, armpit, backbone, waist, hips, legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of this you do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 There was a man who had an arrow or spear pierce his neck root:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I pulled it out from the other side under the ear fat, and he was immediately sensible without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	 And pulled out with play an arrow that pierced the oil sac under the paper under, and the arrow was curved, and could not be reached but the tip towards the flesh, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, all iron head.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 The play was sensible, and no bad accident happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	 I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with iron heads:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I was a barber, and became subtle until I could do it, and the Christians were healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 And extracted an arrow from a man who was either head or stomach-wounded, and thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	 and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not improve.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 I cut above the arrowhead, and guided it, and extracted it without any bad consequences.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	 And if you wish to a man who has an arrow lodged or back, and the wound is healed over.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And the arrow remained within him, and did not disrupt his natural state, nor did it harm any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	 And to another man who had an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound was healed over.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	 It endures thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	 and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	 And draw an arrow from the body of the king, who was lying in bed, and he was slightly tilting to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	 and the arrow was fully inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 I was summoned for treatment after she had been lying there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 Found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	 I felt her entire body with a delicate probe but did not feel any sensation;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 And he felt the tip and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	 I thought it was the arrow tip, so I applied a healing plaster attractifet digestif because the wound was not inflamed.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 The wound of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	 I apply the plaster for many hours, and straighten the wound directly, and let the patient stay like that for a long time until he feels the arrow within his neck daily.
et il le me dist.	 and he told me it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I put the wound on medicine that is corrosive by hand for many hours until it is healed, and then I tried it and felt the head of the arrow which was sticking at its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	 Then I opened the wound with this corrosive medicine until the arrowhead appeared clearly visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 And it healed well within the four-month limit, and then when I cut open the wound with the pliers which I had placed on it from both sides, it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 Therefore, I continued to refine and devise methods for tools, until I took the hour when the tweezers were well made, as their shape will come at the end of this chapter, while pulling it out and returning the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	 And the wise men judge that the nose cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 I will then restore it, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	 Or I told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, but you set your care upon that which I did not say, for books cannot grasp everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 But the wise masters understand little things and what is present and lacking, they discover nine works, and nine instruments, in the reduction of foreign matters that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows are not inserted into limbs where they are fixed except according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 or through the side, or from another angle.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and that which jumps forth at the place where it enters is an arrow penetrating into fleshy parts, and jumps out occasionally.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh is pierced around, and straighten out the exit.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 And if it is fixed in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and move it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And then it jumps out, and if it does not jump out, perforate all around with a sharp instrument until the flesh around is expanded, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	 And if the arrow is driven into the skull bone and reaches one of the brain ventricles, and some of the incidents that I have said openly to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 Do not draw it out immediately, but let it stay as is for some days, for if the arrow reaches so far (to the brain), that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow has not been lodged deep into the bone but only slightly, and the patient experiences no severe incident and remains for some days, you should devise a means to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	 And if it is deeply lodged and cannot come out by itself, administer leeches around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	 If the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, seek it thoroughly;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 and if you feel it, pull it out with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	 And if it cannot be due to the narrowness of the wound, and the deepness of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then open it as wide as possible.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	 Draw the arrow if possible, and if it has ears like an animal and holds there, remove the flesh that is embedded on both sides as far back as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, until you can draw it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And be careful not to break the arrow, but rather pull it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot pull it out in one go, push the linen cloth around it until it is reached the joints, then pull it gently, as the extraction should be done carefully.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	 And if the flow of blood opposes you, bring what we have said in the chapter on its treatment;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	 And beware of incising the nerve or vein, and make an instrument as you know how to draw out the arrow safely, quickly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 Place the patient according to his form when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid that can be, and if you cannot, do so as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 The arrow coming from another place, opens anything of it, or the skin is swollen nearby as we can see or feel apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 Therefore cut through it, as long as the pliers can grasp it, and then pull it out:
si saut fuer maintenant.	 If the arrow is now gone.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then continue extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 And if it is of the arrow shaft, push it all out.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	 If it is a dislocation, and you see the need to administer a traction, then administer the instrument of traction so that the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 Then push forcefully, and if the arrow is entangled, administer the instrument at the tip entering in, to make extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is touched (by the forceps), it is necessary that you cut around where the venom is, as much as possible, then treat the wound as required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	 If the arrow is stuck in the head or face or abdomen or bladder or side, and it is accessible, and you can cover it, then cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	 And be careful to not pierce the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to extract arrows resemble an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	 And there are many ways to do it:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the hair root is similar to the feather of a bird, to guide the point of an arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pointing and straightening is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	incisions of the body common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	 From the veins which one heals there are thirty-one (ways), of which one has sixteen (methods), namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	 The beating that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	 and the two arteries that are in the two temples apparent;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	 and the two veins that are in the two eyelids, which are called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	 and the vein that is under the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	 and the vein that is at the nape of the neck;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	 and the two tendons that are at the neck.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	 and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	 The veins which are commonly cured in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	 One is cephalic, and it lies on the left side of the chest, and the lay people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	 and the middle is called "artery", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the lay people call it "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 and the basilic is on the right side of the chest, and the lay people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the liver, and it is that which is used for bleeding, which opens obviously above the vein.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	 And the little sausage is the vein that is between the ulnar and the radial, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	 And in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	 The first shoulder is located below the curvature of the left ribcage, and the second one that is at the ankle of the right ribcage.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	 and the vein called "nasse," which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And there are three veins underneath those [veins] in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	 The purging of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	 The quality of the purging, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	 Then squeeze the neck of the patient with a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in the two places depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	 Touch the thumb at your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, press firmly on it.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	 Then take the lance, and thrust it through beneath the vein until the bone, then withdraw your hand from the entire vein above, strike and the skin and the vein well two inches through, and make blood come out as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 hold it tight and press until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 and I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	 The healing of the two arteries that are in the temples, is good for migraines, scrofula, and chronic otitis with tears at the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	 And the qualities of the healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	 and it is to stretch out the patient's neck, until both veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	 and feel the pulse beneath your thumb, and then press firmly;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	 then lift the cork on top of the vein toward your index finger, and push the lancet under it, lift the vein upward, and pierce, as you have done in the other veins, and draw blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	 then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it heals.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 And we have spoken about their bandaging and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	 The draining of the vein in the forehead is worth just as much as the draining of the skull in ancient facial diseases that have migrated and turned red.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	 and the quality is that the patient straightens their neck by twisting it until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 then take the tool called "fosseur", whose shape is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	 And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and allow the blood to flow according to the amount that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and not once should one use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	 However, the flames must not be too sharp.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 And the bone is twisted, for it is close; and by chance, the flames break when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	 The salve for the two veins that are in the armpit helps with swelling, and with inflammation, and with scabies, and with earaches, and facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	 and the quality of its salve is that the patient stretches his neck by twisting it in any way, as described before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Then apply the salve, and let the salve be made with a piece of flame about one inch long and wide, for there is no need for charcoal.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	 If the flames are subtle, they may break by chance;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 Then make a poultice of blood, as much as you need, and then apply it on top of cotton, and secure it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	 The vein of the neck serves to cure sickness, scurvy, and diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that come from the face, especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	 And the quality of the vein is such that the patient should compress his neck, then press his neck on your left hand, and take subtle flame long, and insert it between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well in this way, but the pain will begin to recede soon.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	 And do not go too deep, and make the bleeding according to your need, then let it rest for a night, because it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 And this is the form of fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	 The two bindings of the iron aid in the stretching of the bowstring, and at the beginning of tempering, and in many diseases, and in stopping, and in corroding, and in sores, and in stomach ailments.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	 And the quality of the binding is that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	 And the master standing on top of the patient's head, and the patient lies on the seat, then open the vein along its length somewhat widely, then draw out the blood gently, or as much as necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	 Then do the same on the other vein, then untie the ligature, and gently constrict both veins so that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 And let it rest until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the liver surgery
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The translation of the given line is as follows: "The opening of veins in the lips above helps in cooling in the mouth, and in corruption of the gums, and cuts in the lips, and toothache and around."
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	 Then arrange the quality of healing by making the patient sit before you and hold their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	 Then turn the jaw, and look at the two veins, one is on the right jaw and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by the small black veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 Then take hold of both (the veins), and if you do not recognize them and are uncertain about it, grasp the larger one from each side, and also do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for this is the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the liver beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	 The veins below the tongue assist after the cephalic vein is cut, and this is at the incision of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	 And the qualities of the leecher are such that the patient lies between your hands before the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks beneath each side into a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 Then heal both, but do not go too deep, for there are the arteries below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	 The veins from the costal side, which are commonly healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	 or by pricking with sharp, large mirrhin or subtle olive oil as you know it's called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 and they are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of mirrtin flames is very renowned, and it is wide as you see: (Translation)
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	 It is necessary to open the veins that are full of thick blood appearing on the surface, and which contain thick and troubled blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And this is the form of the olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointedly subtle, and is for refining subtle veins with citrus-colored thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	 The basilica's vein, one of these arteries, assists with the diseases that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 And the lord must bleed profusely, and he should let it flow from the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	 If it touches the artery and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And the flame should not be pricked, but rather cut like a nail.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	 If the basilica does not open clearly, then you must open it and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	 Or you wish to take any branch from it, or bleed in its place the vein from the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	 It opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And then hold it in the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	 And if you want to know the location of the vein, then you must also stretch out the arm and feel for the pulse until you find it.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	 Then mark the location of the artery, then tie the arm, and burn the vein with the flame.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	 And be careful not to wound the artery when you see it swelling, for that is the artery:
eschui la donques.	 avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	 And if you see it rise high like the urine of a child, and it is red and thin, know that it is not from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	 Hurry up then, and place your hand firmly on top for a long time, then cut your hand open in multiple places;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	 bind the arm and let it be still, and do not move it for the patient.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and keep it above fear, and do not move it until it is drained.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	 And if it is not drained and swells and the medicine is not present, strike the artery if it is open, for the head of the wound will recede.
et estainche li sans.	 drain the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	 Take a piece of fir bark, cut it in half and place it on top until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	 if the wound is drained, that's good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	 If not, if you treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And the stopping of the bleeding should not be hasty in various positions for the small wound of the injury and the strength of the suture on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	 The evacuation of the vein in the middle helps to treat the blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	 And the surgeon must be careful when searching for the nerve that is below, and if it pricks too deeply and finds the nerve, it inflates and the patient becomes sick, and there may be no healing.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	 And this nerve opens up very often, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must anesthetize the healthy part of the instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 Cut the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	 The incision of the skull helps, because it draws blood from the head and assists the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 And it is necessary to incise at the point of olive oil or myrtle fire, because this is the safest among all veins, since there is neither nerve nor artery below it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	 However, you must seek the most shallow joint and do not press too hard if the first time is necessary, and repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 And by chance, the joint swells in some men when the first time is required, but do not press too hard.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	 The first thing you should know about healing is that healing does not come unless to keep health and avoid upcoming diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	 and the healing shall be done in one of the three veins that are cut:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	 this is to know, cephalic, femoral, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	 and it should be healed at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when the signs of satiety appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 and it should be healed on the first or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	 The healing that is given for diseases does not have a set duration, but when it is necessary day or night, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 It is not necessary to purge children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman during pregnancy except for the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	They should not heal the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	 If anyone wants to purge themselves in any way, it is necessary that their intestines be cleansed with a gentle clysterium, if they have retained many feces, so that the veins do not transport the waste from the intestines and harm the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	 A person who is excessively salted with foods, who is drunk, as long as he is pregnant, or dropsical should not purge themselves.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	 If there is diarrhea after purging, vomiting, distension of the abdomen, excessive abortion in women, much labor, watching and fasting, and those who lose all their strength, or due to something from the weapon or body parts, it is necessary that they rest.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	 Then thin out the humors, if the patient does not have a large amount of them, with food and drinks and medicine, if you have that ability.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	 Then immerse [the affected area], if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood and heal the vein in the affected area around the third, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	 And keep that day from work, and from pain, and from sexual activity, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	 And rest in bed and enjoy yourself, and let the bandages be higher than those of the patient being treated, and rub the arm 2 or 3 times, then gently pull the bandage upwards, because if it is too tight or loose, it cannot heal.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	 And afterwards rub the affected area with your hands until the veins swell and they are felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 Then moisten the incision with a little old oil, then place your thumb of your left hand on that vein beneath the skin as far as you can see the incision, so that the incision does not bleed and fail to be cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	 For there are veins that run like cords for the incision, and some that are filled with pus, such that when you put fire to it, it recoils from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 And if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the incision should be advised in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	 And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 If not (the joint), start again a little below or above that level if it is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	 And if the joint is swollen and the patient fears, let it rest for a day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	 Perhaps abscesses will come out.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	 Do not enter (the wound) or bathe it, then start the healing if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	 And if the wound is small or you doubt that it will not bleed much as you see, trust in that same wound entirely with direct heat.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	 Work a little quickly, so that the joint is swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 For this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	 If you see the joint swollen, do not start treatment immediately. Put a little oil on it, for it cools the body from the blood, and the oil is made in this place where the oil is.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	 And thus administer the oil of oil in every treatment that you treat the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	 and this same thing is triple and hollow from it when it is put on the joint;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 if the blood becomes too thick and spreads out when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	 And if a large abscess comes, which happens frequently, especially when the treatment of the vein is not performed until that time or the opening of the vein is small, hurry, and put a damp sponge on hot water and oil on it on the joint and hold for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	 And it is necessary that you do this after the blood flow from the vein, and if it remains in place after some days without any black or green appearance, it does not matter.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh resin under a hot iron, mastic, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	 And often an abscess and appearance occurs near the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 Put your hand on it then, and if you feel that the place is soft to the pressure of the hand, it is the harmful appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	 Then do not put anything of what has been said, for by chance it may be an artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 But you can use a plaster to harden the place, then treat it with other treatment until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	 If the wound is black, leave it to drain until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	 and if you see a swelling, let it become thin;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	 For the person who is swollen and hollow, and requires bloodletting, make the incision larger, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	 And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it must be bled lightly and often, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And this method of bleeding avoids the displacement of blood and the compression of nerves, and is better than bleeding deeply rather than widely.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	 And to the one whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give soft bread under ripe pomegranates.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 If it is scalded, let blood three or four times; and if of cold complexion, before healing eat soft bread in syrup sweetened, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, chives, and a pleasant-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if the hand is wounded after much bleeding, then it must be treated with burnt charcoal, a fragrant subtle syrup, and other things as mentioned in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If one wants to fracture his arm, and heal it again at another time, if it is weakened by repeated healing, then let him heal little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to fracture his arm after the first healing, and has a strong body, let him heal in 6 hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal from another part, should heal on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	 For there is much blood within the body which is already scalded, causing fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	 Therefore, a large amount must be let out, and the hole widened until it chooses to emit in a cloth.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	 Then, having prepared all the conditions for healing, place your hand on top of the cloth when it heals so that death does not come in its place, and this happens many times when healers are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	 And it is not necessary that when you dislocate the arm and draw blood a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	 nor if it's bent, stretch out the arm as much as possible, for that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	 but leave it until it bleeds a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 or you touch it with the tip of the flame until the congealed blood flows out of the vein and put on the piece of linen kept in vinegar, and press slightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to draw blood a second time, draw it from the same place, or another vein, or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are opened at the location of the neck because they are composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	 And the method of bleeding is that the patient immerses his hand in hot water until the flesh becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	 then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then bleed now across the palm, neither too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	 And make the wounds large, and cauterize them closely near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be drained, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow out into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	 And if it is frozen, do not push the hand into hot water, because it is put more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the cauterization of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	 The cauterization of the tendon of the right hand is useful for all liver diseases, and this is how it works:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	 Hold the hand, put it in hot water until the vein has burst open, if you can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	 And if the incision is transverse, and you cover it entirely all over, it causes no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 And do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath all uncovered with flesh; then place the hand in hot water, if the wound does not freeze and cannot heal.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as necessary, put oil and wax on the wound to heal quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgative of the hand on the left side is beneficial for the disease of mice, and do as I have told you regarding the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The salve of the thigh is effective for all diseases under the body, such as diseases of the belly, retention of fluids, kidney diseases, and old leg and knee diseases, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	 And the quality of his wound is that the patient should thrust his foot into hot water and rub over the vein until it perishes, and bind above the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	 And the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot go very deep.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 Therefore open it more widely or as large as at the ankle, for it will heal quicker.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	 And if you open the wound above the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and make an incision transversely as when cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the limb cannot come out, put it in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	 And if it is necessary to apply leeches for the first time, then start with the second one a little, because the flesh is salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the soothing of the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee of fire, and its lesion is worth the pain of the hinge when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	 And the quality of his leeches is that the patient enters or bathes, and draws above the ankle 4 fingers in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	 And if it opens, then draw out in all ways that you can, and by crossing over.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 It is better to cut it off, for the flesh is rotten, and it responds well to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	 And if you do not heal it, no remedy will open or close the thigh bone, and turn towards the little finger, and beware of nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	 Make such a pressure on the blood that you see, then cut the ligament, put cotton on it and press.
ele est maintenant sanee.	 It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of suction cup remedies
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Blisters are made of horn, or hare, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	 And blistering is done according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 or by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	 And this blistering that is done without wounding can be done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 It is to all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 and ventilation which is made by wounding and the extraction of blood if it is done in 14 inches on the body, so the one who is entirely in summer (the head) is affected.
et li autres est emmi le col;	 and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	 and the others in the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	 and the ventous (boils) under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	 and the boils of the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	 and the boils on the legs;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	 and the boils in the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	 and the boils of the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 and the boils on the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	 and ventilation does not deal with blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it should not be doubted at all, if as with opening of a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And it should not be administered, neither at every fire nor with fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	 If by necessity of diseases it is required to apply leeches, or according to custom, we will administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle and at every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	 for there are those who, when they need to apply leeches, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	 and to those who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	 and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and are bleeding;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if there are some who think, and see by no blood and boils and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially if it is outside of the month, we command to ventose after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	 The mouthwash helps with the pain in the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that it should be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	 and this ventilation is in place of the mouthwash for the headache ... and it is not necessary that those who are of cold constitution should use it, or who have catarrh, because it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 And for this reason, it is not necessary that the guards should use it, nor those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves often become careless and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the danger of negligence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	 Ventilation around the neck is in place of the mouthwash for the head and basilica, and for this reason it is effective against the stiffness, and splitting of the channel of the worm, and swelling, and fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 And it should not be held too tightly, for if it remains firmly pressed, it may cause obstinacy or stomach and heart ailments.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	 The ventosations in the ribs of the neck are worth the pains of the head, and otalgia and migraines, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the sanctuary of Basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 And you should instruct the lord to press his hand gently, not to crush the artery, and not let blood come out excessively.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	 The ventosation under the chin is worth the mouth diseases, and corruption of gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 And it is in the place of the sanctuary of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations of the shoulders are useful for disease caused by heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	 The ventosations of the ribs are as much as three veins from the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 And command the lord not to make too deep an incision, because the bone is naked with flesh, and hides nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	 The ventose (ventilation) above the buttocks is worth as many fistulas from the foundation, and diseases beneath it; and the ventose should be large and made of copper, because it needs to draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	 And in case it is subtle (thin), it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	 It causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	 The ventoses of the legs open widely because they draw blood from all over the body, and are worth ancient pains in the back, and in the testicle, and bladder, and reduce swellings.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 And they are in the positions of the shoulders, and the elbows, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and bring palsy in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	 The method of putting on the cupping glass is that you put it first empty, suck it quickly, place it hastily, move it equally, and do not stop doing so until you see the area turn red and inflated, and the redness of the blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	 Then cool it down, and apply the cupping glasses, and take care in the placement of the body, for there are some who have tender flesh and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	 It is necessary to cut only once, and make large incisions, and a small deep one.
et suce legierement.	 Suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	 If it isn't swollen, then it should be struck twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 The first time is to thin the way of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	 And if it is very swollen, then it should be struck a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And when we want to draw the blood drop by drop, we only need to pierce it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	 And if we want a lot of blood, then we reward it often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	 And if the swelling is large, we pierce completely and make sure that the arteries are punctured suddenly; this is for those with thick skin and hard flesh, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the sides of the veins with stimulating and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	 If it is oil of violets, olive oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of seed from a gourd:
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 and if it is linseed oil, watercress oil, iris oil, chamomile oil, or any similar:
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amoradine oil, or balm of Gilead oil, or anise oil, and others similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if one who is to be healed has to stretch out tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be put on it, but it should be washed after the ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of morels, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or any similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from asses' milk, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 And those with excessive fluidity rise up from old wine or sour water, or decoction of fennel or chamomile, or any similar:
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 and it is not necessary to bleed with a lancet before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two:
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 and he must not sleep after bleeding, and it is necessary that he urinate, when he needs to bleed and when he has bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 And be aware that if the person who is healing is coleric, and he lacks temperament and is excessively inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 then he must take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in moderation, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 and eat spicy foods, and meat of young rooster, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And if he has a cold constitution, he should take honey syrup, moderately fragrant wine, which is neither old nor new, and eat little, and spicy foods and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 and on the day he will vomit, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 it is necessary to give some men three times tracle or muscatel before vomiting, or after, to strengthen the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And let the drink be refined, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The blisters placed over wounds are those placed on the liver, the spleen, gout, abdomen, flanks and loins, because these parts do not bear being cut open, and it is done for no other reason than to draw blood from one member into another, such as we place them over the breasts when a woman is menstruating.
