por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 To remove the viscosity from the limb, as we do by placing leeches on the abdomen and the buttocks to reduce it.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 and alleviate pain when there is obstruction or a foreign body, as it draws out the obstruction by chance, or dislodges the arrow from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 and in this manner it performs when placed on the liver and the spleen where there is retained fluidity, and these leeches are administered empty to suck as little as possible.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 Sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this manner the leech is filled with hot or cold water to which cooked herbs such as comfrey have been added.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the bladder administered to fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 And it should be two fingers and half a palm in length, and have an opening of about one millimeter around the middle, like pushing a needle, and made of steel, soft enough before so as not to prick the patient when placed on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 and have a rod of steel or iron for the purpose of applying a plaster, and it should be large or small according to the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 for the sores of children are different from those of the old and thin from those that are fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And this plaster should be placed thus on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 Take the plaster of wax or lint and place it in the plaster inside the rod that is inside the plaster, so that the light is at the bottom of the plaster so as not to burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 And then place it on the member, and your fingers should be over the wound as we have said, so that when one looks at it, if there is steam, remove the bladder.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 Take a thread and repeat the suturing often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the bladder given for the disease of pleurisy, in all acute cases, there should be no needle or wound, and it should not be brought unless when it is full of liquid, and it should only be placed on the member.
et c’est li forme:	 and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Bladders are not brought except for members where it is not possible to place bladders due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 And in bare muscles, as with thighs or similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 and the qualities of the patient are such that when you find bladder stones in sweet clear waters, you can take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 and put them into clean sweet water, until they become familiar and have no air in them;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 and then pierce with a vein and a bladder, then rub the member until it is red, and put the bladders on them.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 And when they are full and hot, if it is a place where a bladder can be placed, put it there because it works well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If it cannot be done, lift the area and clean it with water, then press it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 And if the limb heals too long after the body, soak the linen cloth in cold water and place it on, until the wound is dried.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 And if the wound multiplies, place broken glass or similar things on it until it dries.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 Or put half-peeled beans on the limb and leave them until they adhere to the limb, it will dry now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 And if you have more need of it, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the wounds do not want to take, rub fresh blood on the limb or insert a needle into the wound until it bleeds, then place them on and as soon as they feel the blood, they adhere.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see that they (plural, referring to the eyes) are weeping, sprinkle a little bit of aloe powder and crushed camomile or ashes on them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Know, dear child, that the foolish man who suffers from this chapter will never see any of the old books or read any letters in them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 And because of this reason, the art (science) is alienated from our land, for I have never found anyone good in it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 And I know nothing about it (the art), except by the science of the old books that I have studied so much that I have treated it, and by experimentation, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 And I have described in this chapter what is contained within it and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to say the prologue of this book the summary of speech and chapters where wise men put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who have experience know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain occurs to anyone, it is necessary that you treat the patient from both sides, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infants, or elderly.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 or if the time is not very warm, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 and avoid cold foods, namely raw meats, and consume cool drinks and vegetables, do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about abscess heat or spreading of matter to the member.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 if the patient returns to his first government he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that make thick broths, or they have thickness, such as cooked wheat in water, and meat of the head, and feet, and pancreas of cow, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	In prolonged nursing, the wounds break more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well regained or joined according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 but there is no healing, reset the broken bone on top of the large tendons that pierce and join the limb together, as forcefully as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 and do not let him at all work, and for this reason, he must be fed large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are different in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is different than the break of the arm or leg; I will tell you all the ways of a break in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that heal by growing together like the quill of a pen when writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if the break has an open wound, and the break is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And in every way have his device and instrument appropriate for the restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 And it is known that the fracture of the bone occurs when the joint is twisted and opened wide by pulling apart, and it is compressed with the press of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 And when it has no twisting or crookedness, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no breakage.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 But it may have twisting, or a fracture, or a small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand at all, but place medicines that come after here, and then hold it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 Know that the breaks which grow into ulcers, and are the two parts dislocated, you must now set them equally, otherwise abscesses will grow there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 And if abscesses come close, you should leave it for some days until the abscess subsides;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 Then set it equally to the muscle that you can easily and skillfully move, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration where there are pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 Then hold steady, as needed hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 And if the bone is broken into pieces and split in two, whether it be of the hand or foot, or with one hand for small members, or by using two ropes, or with one rope and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 And place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the member are disconnected, reset them with all devices in their joints as you can, and ensure by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 Align well the two bones properly according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 Feel it with your hand if it seems not to be right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 If it is well aligned, do not strain it too much nor press as those who cause abscess and contraction in the member by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 When the member is set, punish the patient so he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And keep the limbs so secure that they feel no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 For when it feels no pain, it is not in place, and it must be set in such a way that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 And ensure that it is placed correctly, so that deformities do not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members vary in smallness and in size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small members such as arms and fingers and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	 It is necessary to wrap linen cloths that are soft and thin.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	 And for those that are thick, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	 It is necessary to wrap with a thick and hard cord, because the wide cords encase the whole large member, and restrain it evenly on all sides so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 Then tie light bandages around it three or four times according to the member, and hold your hand slightly on the joint, then go above the fracture and apply less pressure, so that the fracture contracts a little, then move the fracture away a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	 Soften the joint slowly, taking a large part of the healthy limb, then take another bandage and turn it around the broken limb in the opposite direction.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 then return to the part below the fracture and apply moderate pressure, neither too hard nor too gently, as we said in the first line above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 Then put soft bandages of linen or cloth between the joints so they are even, then tie everything above with the bandage, and then place your splints well made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 And if there is swelling or abscess, place a soothing hot substance on it, and who removes the swelling, leave it for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 then hold your arms steady, and they should be about half the width of a thick cane wrapped tightly, or a plank like that used for splitting wood, or palm branches, and in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 but the arm that one places over the fracture should be a little thicker and larger than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 and be as long as necessary for the small or large limb;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then hold your arms steady again as you did at the first stage, then tie them with a cord going upwards, as you did on the fracture in the first stage.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 The more narrow it [the joint] becomes, the less wide it will be.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 because if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their cords from twisted flax, and that is a great error, for the knots cannot be even if it is too delicate; moreover, there should not be less than the width of two fingers' space between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient has been struck by the heads of arrows in their joints after they have been set straight in healthy ones, place linen or cotton poultices over them so that they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bones are broken, I shall tell the cure below after that.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to set all fractured limbs at once on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	 For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to make holes for stitches before the fifth day or the seventh, or more according to your certainty of abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 And here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 And you take flour that is kept near the mill walls and mix it with an abundance of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it; this is the common method for restoring a fracture in various ways, and especially for women and small children, as it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Another way of applying plaster to restore the fracture, dislocation, and sprain:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take a lancet and linen cloth and alum and asafetida and Arabic gum, mix in X quantities;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 myrrh and aloeswood, in V quantities;
alechil VIIII З.;	 The shoulder blade (alecil) should be set back nine times;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 and make powder from it, and mix it with egg yolk;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 If the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, as it has a good composition, and restore broken bones quickly, and helps many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another type of plaster for twisting (torsion) relief:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	 Take mugwort and vismil, in nine parts;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 myrrh and aloes, in eight parts;\]   pois les moule et les metes en une paille a fumier;
acaice VI З.;	 The dislocation is caused by some disjointing from its place, therefore it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned; this causes the patient great pain and injury.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Break well and grind finely, boil with vinegar or an abundance of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another way to apply plaster for dislocated joints and displaced bones, alleviate the pain that occurs, and cut away the bone, break it.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take new linen, soak it in boiled oil and water, and put it on top of the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This bandage does not restore [the joint or bone], but it is good for alleviating the abscess heat and bone pains properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another way to apply plaster for bones that are broken and displaced:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried fig leaves and purslane leaves, grind them together to make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of bandaging for the restoration of the fractured bone and for hastening the healing of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take root of comfrey, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wormwood, from each one a part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the limbs are burned, apply to it moist coriander water or vinegar, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of emplastrum (medical ointment or paste) stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take roots of comfrey, flax seeds, balm of Gilead, sweet clover and witch hazel, flowers of violets and chamomile, all together in equal parts.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 grind, and make into a paste with salt water, sweet water or wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates wrote in his book that no other substance should be placed on a broken member for restoration except for an ointment made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems Galen says that dry and somewhat warm things should be placed on a broken member for restoration, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Another way of poultice that helps for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Grind up muggath and horsehairs from shaved men or feathers of birds, and equal amounts of alum, and sieve them, and make a plaster with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 Then wait a little while after that, and ensure the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 If it is not dislocated for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 But if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry and dislocate it, remove the plaster now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 Take a light cloth and sea sponge dipped in water, lift the place, until the itching stops and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place dry linen on it, dampen it with vinegar or rose oil, and tie it up tightly until you are sure the abscess is hot.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 And let the inflammation of the limb rest and the pain be removed, then begin wrapping it subtly, using a little emplastrum, and do not strain it too much as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has healed and turned red, swollen, hot, and sore, and you need plaster and linen, apply it as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, do not remove the binding before three or four or five or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 And sometimes leave it for twenty days, as one sees fit, until the bone breaks and the wound heals over.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 Then stretch it more than before, and make its flesh thicker, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 If you see the joint drying out too much, know that nutrients cannot reach it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 Warm it with hot moist heat every time you dislocate it, and do so three times a day, and loosen the joint slightly.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 By this means, cut off the nutrients to the limb, and quickly heal what fools leave twisted.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 It is bad, and it is fearful work, and I see nothing but laboring and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 There are many types of breaks, and various shapes, and the causes are intended for different things.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 For there are breaks made by the impact of swords, and the collar bone fractures all the way up to the shaft which is beneath the bone, as a hacksaw or club does;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 and for this reason, such break is called "hackbreak".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 Or if the sword strikes the bone from above in such a way that it pierces through, this kind of break is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 And these two breaks are large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a percussion buried, or a cleft or shaft of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or it is on the bone itself, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And if the wound is closed in the bone as thin as hair, and it is a small fracture, it is called "hairline".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or anything similar, and it drives a bone fragment inside, and the joints are crushed as blacksmiths do on top of the cauldrons;
si entre li piere dedens.	 If (something) enters into the bone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And this happens more often in those with moist bones, like a child's head.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 It also occurs in all these ways of breakage, where small pieces are dislocated, like splinters.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 I shall speak about its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the exploration with probing, and by corruption of the flesh that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy appearance is known to those who, when they have uncovered the bone and rub it vigorously, make the fracture blacken.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of the patient's condition, and if you see any unfavorable circumstances, such as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, paleness, high fever, hairs appearing and turning red, and other signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no unfavorable circumstances and hope for a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the navroz comes first to you, and it is in winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the start of menstruation.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is not corrupted, and come the complications as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the bone break comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, you must cut open the fractured part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 And you are to take the head of the patient and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound make it softer than possible, and if a discharge of blood comes out when exposing the bone or an abscess appears, you should help it with what is necessary; and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 And make the wound rest until the abscess has subsided, and ensure the flow of blood is stopped.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 Then begins the bone to cut out, and it is done according to two ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 The first way is that you cut in a narrow incision in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 The second way is that you have different numbers of incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed, and made with sharp iron tools.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 And work gently, so as not to cut the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 If the bone is hard and protruding, you must drill around it so that you can make incisions with chisels, but not cutting through the bone to the other side, and above the point it should have a margin or circle, which prevents the point from passing through the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 And you must have several, so that each one comes into its place on the end of the bone, so that you have trepan(s) for all purposes.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 This is the form of the three kinds of trepans (trepan instruments):
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The qualities for trepanning around the broken bone are that you place the trepan on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 Then place the trepan elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the fractures, and do this as subtly and lightly as you can, and carefully, as we have said, until you extract the bone with your hand or any tool you have, such as pliers or tweezers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 Keep in mind you are not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 Once the bone is pierced and treated, it is necessary to reset the dislocation that remains within the bone with an instrument resembling a pair of pliers, but it should be thinner and more delicate than other pliers.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 And if there is something remaining of the small bones, or scales, gently remove them with instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 Then treat the wound with cautery and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 The other way of work, which is more dangerous, is the one that Galen described.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 He very strongly advises it, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must cut open a part of the bone where the fracture is visible, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place under it the head of the curved incision, which has the shape shown below.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And it does not cut completely through from one side, and the parts are sharp on two edges, so that the cutting is toward the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly cut through the bone all around, and take care of the cloth that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 if it is close to the bone, cut lightly, because cutting too deeply can cause harm and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone does not break through to the cloth, and the bone is chipped only from above, and there are small pieces, then you must do this after roughing it up, and remove the scales with a sharp razor of various sizes, in order to make available the most suitable one for each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	The patient should shave off large areas of hair, then proceed to finer razoring, and continue this process until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	 In each of the other hair-like cuts and subtle breaks, you should bring to the surface according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 this is something not easily answered by one who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	 And if the wound is exposed, you should take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	 Then take another cloth folded in two or three, wet it with wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	 and do it more gently than you can, so as not to weigh down the wound, then administer it through another layer, and do not strain it any further than necessary to touch only the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	 and leave it thus for a day or two until the abscess is soothed, then release it, and administer medicines like those of lilies, flour of wheat, incense powder, arsenic, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	 and make powder from these things, put it on the wound, and administer immediate medicine without masticication (chewing).
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	 And be careful that the wound is always clean, do not leave any dressing or pack it with bandages, for when the packing is assembled on the brain cloth, it will rot and corrupt, causing great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 For if you put anything sharp on it, it will burn through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be careful to avoid any bad accidents happening to the patient as we have said, for it is doubtful and full of doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	 And if blackness does not come forth except for the medicine that has been put on it, having this property, you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, mix them together with linen cloth and apply it to the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal it in the manner of wounds that is appropriate, until it heals completely.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	 Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one part alone, because they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 And below is cartilage, and it does not break, but it does not cause swelling or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	 And if one of the two parts is broken, you must break your little finger or thumb nail, and insert it equal to the break inside the index finger, and to the palm by the side, until the nail regrows according to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is in the part above the nose and the thumb cannot reach the place, you should place it equal to the top of a small rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	 If the break is between two parts, you should repair it similarly, and hurry to restore it within a day if possible.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then apply bandages of linen to the tip of the nail if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	 When you step on another from another side, it breaks there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 and the tents be as thick that they fill the holes in the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said any remedy that one should soak tents in butter and churn them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	 It does not seem good to me, but they should be moistened in the making of egg yolk and flour powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 Then let the tent remain until the bone is hard and the cartilages harden.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	 And sometimes people step on goose pen feathers instead of tents, and if the wound is covered with linen cloth, and hold the breakage, and blow into the patient.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 or do what you want to do.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess occurs while you are working on it, put either cotton soaked in rose oil or a small piece of camphor on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	 If an abscess does not come, apply plaster on the outside, with flour of lime and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then put light stops on it and do not bind the neck.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	 And if the break in the neck is small, and it breaks into many small pieces, extract the fragments with suitable instruments, then make an incision, and treat with substances that are healing such as plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there is no wound within the neck, treat it with linen strips, and place woolen bands on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	If the jawbone is fractured without any external wound and the break is not split in two but only displaced, and if it's recognized easily that it's just displaced, not broken completely inside, as can be seen from the curve.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	 It is necessary that you insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient if the break is in the right part.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 And if the break is in the left lower jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand gently into the opening, and adjust it with the other hand from outside, and hold it steady.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two places, you should provide extension to both places equally.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	 And if movement of the teeth occurs, or breaking, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a broken jaw bandage on it and place a double cloth on top.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 Place a big bandage or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it in place where you can, and tell the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	 If you see that the figure changes, dislocate it the next day, and then reset it where it is changing.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	 Place a plaster on it with milled powder with plenty of egg or flour of lime after removing the bandage.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	 And put a light linen cloth on the dislocation, and if it swells, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it until it heals.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 Often it heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess arises, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	 If there is a fracture and wound together, tie up any piece of the bone that has been removed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 Choose the most suitable instrument for removing the bone piece.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, expand it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is no more left, then close the wound, if it is wide, and apply one dressing suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the bandage
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	 The break is often made several times towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	 or it is broken and disjointed at the second joint, and it has parts, and it is the easiest to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 and there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	 And the work if the fracture is accompanied by a wound, you should have two attendants, so that one presses the shoulder where the bone seems broken.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	 And the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 Then equal the break at your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor deformation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	 And if you need to stretch more, put a round ball of fabric or linen on the patient under the shoulder, and it should be large according to your need.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 Stretch and raise the armhole, hold the ball in place with your hand, and straighten the break as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder outward due to its being deep-set, as it comes in deeply, then the patient must lie on his affected side, and place one ear against the shoulder, and push the shoulder downward, until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	 Then direct the break at your fingers, and if you find that it is broken, you must cut over it.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	 Pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined in any way, strike it at one of the incisions you have made.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 But you put it under the forceps for traction.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	 and appears like a spoon, not concave, and be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	 and it should have two arms, as you see, and one wide and the other narrow, as is the incision of the wound that you made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 and when you are sure of the abscess being hot, if the wound is closed, and the incision is small, or if you doubt the abscess being hot, if the wound is closed, use linen cloths and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if pustules become hot, soak a cloth in rose oil, asafoetida, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	 The setting of the bone, when it feels like there are wounds and sawing, is that you place on the bone the plaster made from milled powder and egg white, apply light stops, and put a sphere under the assemble if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	 Then take a very long bandage of one palm width, then place a double cloth on top of hot iron, and apply it.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	 Then take a thin stick of three feet long and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage protrudes.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	 and place the stick on the broken bone, turn the bandage around the neck, and press down healthy flesh, and press down sick flesh.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	 and separate each part, and when you see that the bones are healing properly and it is clear that the stick does not move above the broken bone, keep it in place every day, and if the swelling subsides, hold it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	 And make the patient lie down on his back, and place a small pillow under his buttocks to raise the shoulder.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	 Align the fracture of the forearm by aligning the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck and do not untie it except in case of a bad accident for twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	 Then repeat the plastering, if you see that it is necessary, and bind it and leave it like this until it heals.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 And it will heal within twenty-eight days at the most, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	 It seldom happens that a broken or dislocated shoulder does not heal, and it should not be forced unless by touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 If the fracture appears according to its break's figure, and you reset it according to its natural form in all ways possible;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	 then put on the joint powder from the mill with abundant egg and light plasters, and place it on a double cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	 then place a broad and fine awl, a bit larger than the shoulder, and under the awl is the hollow part of the shoulder in any position; if there are no cavities around the shoulder, use linen plasters so that the awl pierces evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	 and then hold it tightly with a strong bandage so that the awl does not move from its place, and observe the ligament every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	 And every time it breaks, hold it in place, and align the bone if it is out of its place, and make the patient lie on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	 The shoulder will be reset within twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 And when this number is completed, release it, and be careful, for the bone does not move easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes before and not beneath the skin, lift it up, remove it, and do as we have said in the treatment of an abscess to cool it.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture by the wound
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	 The arm is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 but it often breaks at the elbow.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 When it is broken through the middle, it declines below and causes the patient great pain, lack of alignment, suddenness, and occasionally vomiting blood, and the fractured bone opens widely, and it feels bad everywhere.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	 The restoration is that the patient lies on his back, places the cushion between his shoulders, then presses the shoulders and assembles the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and subtly align in all ways possible until the shape of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	 Then place plasters and poultices over the subtle stick of salt or another light staff, and wrap it in a cloth, and hold it on the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	 And turn the rope tightly around the back, and tighten it gradually, and each hour inspect the knot, and if it loosens, tighten it again.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	 and if it is necessary to undo the rope, due to corrosion or pruritic irritation at the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, undo it, remove the plaster, and direct those who have come for treatment in a suitable manner.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then reset the plaster and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	 Know that the fracture of ribs occurs only in large ones, after the back and inside the chest, and they do not bend except for when they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 and it is felt well at the examination with fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 The restoration is that you make the break even again, as necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 And then put a splint and bind it with a stick if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	 And if the fracture of ribs is inclined downwards, the patient feels very great pain and shortness of breath, just like in pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lining.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 It protrudes with points and quickly and vomits a great amount of blood, and it is a grave illness, and they used to apply much effort in treating the old.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that distend the belly, in order to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot irons come, unless they have arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have arrived, we heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	 And some of them said that bladders are placed on the wound, to suck it out, and it seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 Always, there is fear that the bladder does not draw superfluidities to their place due to weakness of position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And it was said by some that one should cover the wound with damp linen soaked in hot oil and put plasters between the ribs to make the wound evenly healed, then it is cured with a cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	 And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone which does not pass through the wall, and fear is present for the patient, then it is necessary to break above the area of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put something under it to support it;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then you must cut the bone and pull it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	 And when an abscess comes to the surface, put wet linen soaked in rose oil on it and cover the area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And treat as needed the place where it should be incised, and let it lie swabbed on the side where it is, until it becomes healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	 Sometimes breaks occur in the neck bones, and often they bend.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 And similarly to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens and you want to know if it will heal or not, take note if his hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and he cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel pain.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in various positions, and if they are mute and can feel when stretched or pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient should be healed if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	 And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, take care if the feet are numb, and if there are accidents that are in hands, and sudden back spasms and movements against one's will.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And when it has been swabbed on the stomach, sudden movement occurs against one's will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And if it has been sustained on the back and you want to relieve it, you cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	 Note that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Do not labor at all in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen to him, it will be a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	 And the treatment is to warm it if there is an abscess that is hot, apply rose oil or oil of egg yolk until it is soothed.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	 Then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices and tie it with a string, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And do not sleep on that part where there is pain until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	 And if any bone is dislocated, it must be covered with oil.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Break the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound if it is large, with stitches, then heal it with soothing ointment until it is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	 And if the shoulder blade is broken, which is called "the shoulder of the cow," push your left hand's knuckles against it and align them with the other hand as you can, then put the splint and the stick above it if needed.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Then straighten it, and if there is bone displacement, raise it, and set the bone and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the shinbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	 It rarely happens that the bone of the shin is broken, and if it does happen, there is only a slight reduction in the pain at the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 And they make it long, bend it toward the inside, and bring pain to the patient at the place, prick it, and swell that which is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	 And the repositioning is such that you stretch out your hand above, while you are at the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	 and know what the break and its shape is;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	 if the break is only in the head, then equalize that break, while it remains in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or bends inside, then lay the patient on his stomach so that the restoration of the fracture may be apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	 And when you have made it even, put on a plaster and then a splint of wood or horn, and hold the break still so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	 place the arm below the ribs, until the joint is equalized.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on the unaffected side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 If an abscess swells there, do not touch it until the swelling has subsided, and place on what we have previously mentioned.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	 And then return to the restoration, hold it as required, if there is no bad incident.
et c’est li maniere.	 This is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	 The shoulder joint is that which is between the neck and the upper arm, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 One method is to take a large splint, in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	 And tie the heads together with two ropes, and raise them up, and place the patient on a chair.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	 Then lay the broken arm on the splint, until it is in place, and have a curve of splint in the middle, then raise it up to some heavy object or the assistant extends it downwards.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 Then put the mirror the equalizer in his hands together, until the equalizer returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to place the patient on his side and tie his arm to his neck, then command two assistants that one holds the broken part with his hands above, and the other holds the rod below with one cord and extends each part to its own side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 If you see that the extraction is too strong, hold the ligament beneath the break, and above the break, and extend each of the assistants to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	 If the equalizer is close to the shoulder, then you must place the middle link below the socket and the other towards the skin, under the equalizer;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	 and similarly if the equalizer is towards the skin, then place the link gently, without effort, so that the equalizer is even on the joint and on the skin.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 Then make the dislocation equal as it should be, and hold it steady if abscesses do not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	 If abscesses come out, do not hold it steady for more than 7 days, and put soft linen on it with rose oil until the abscesses are calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	 Then hold the shoulder in place, and the way to do so is that you place the elbow on the dislocation, then move the arm towards the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.
