And place the cloth, then hold the shoulder in place towards the shoulder, so that the arm is in its socket, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not dislocated.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	 And if you doubt that the bone is not dislocated, use a splint, and place on the dislocation a larger and stronger splint than the others, with a space of 2 fingers between each splint, and make each splint so large that it passes over the dislocation by 3 fingers on either side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 Hold firmly on the joints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter concerning fractures, more firmly and less in loosening them.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if you see the position of the joints and tightening, as we have said, during the time you are restoring the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave it to heal for seven days as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 Then examine every three days the wound, to ensure that inflammation does not occur or come to the place, or the pus cannot enter the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	 And if no such accident occurs, do not remove the bandage until three days or more have passed, and let the patient lie on his back, and keep his hands on his stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	 And place a splint under the shoulder equally thick with linen, and observe every hour of the day or night that the broken member does not move, or the ligaments are not softened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	 if the advice is given by the virtue of medicine, and meat is given which we have previously specified, so that the meat is initially fine.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 and when it begins to regain strength, it can be made thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be restored in forty days in total.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And then you must release it and administer baths and ointment-medicine for its alignment.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the structure (of the shoulder) is deformed and swollen, it remains to loosen it for several days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "double bones", of which one is small and it is the one that follows the elbow.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	 And the others [are] large, and this one is beneath, toward the small hole.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 Occasionally only the large one breaks, or the small, and sometimes both together break.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	 When the small bone is broken, the restoration and healing are easy.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 And when the large one is broken, the healing is poor, and more difficult than when they break together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only the small fracture has been broken, it should be slightly extended and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	 If it is the large bone, it must be pulled harder;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	 and stretch it towards the wrist, lift the thumb of the hand higher than the others, let the small one lower than the others, and let the patient lie crosswise on himself, and let the wrist be above him, so that the patient suffers no labor;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 Then the ministers extend their arms to the part below the hand, or at the elbow, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then set the patient straight, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there is a fracture in pieces, put each one in its place; and if any of them has slipped out, pricks the keyhole, and you cannot restore it to its place, then saw through and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	 And as for breaking an abscess, I have spoken about it in a separate chapter.
si pren la cure.	 Take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	 If at the beginning of restoration, abscesses appear raw, apply the dressing made of rose oil and white beeswax, not too hard or too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 and place the dressing gently on top until the raw abscess is soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	 Then remove the beeswax and apply the poultice of milled powder with egg, then place the hot stones, and the stone for breaking should be stronger and slightly larger than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	 And know that he must have 6 or more bones or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	 either the break is in one of the bones, or two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	 and hold the fracture higher than elsewhere, and at all times less when aligning, as I said at the beginning of the chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	 let the bandages that are above the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 and let the thread, with which it is held together, be of flax, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And hold the member and the joint afterwards for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	 If any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must irrigate the limb with hot water until the itching is relieved.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 Allow the limb to rest, do not restrain it.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then continue the bandaging, and if the ligaments are damaged and the bones dislocated, or similar things, take care to do so.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the urine cannot reach the member because it is too narrow, so that it does not pass through, then you must soften it with a poultice for a short time, and leave it like this for some days until the urine flows through, and then bandage it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things mentioned above happen to the patient, do not release him until twenty days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	 Meanwhile, bind his hands to his neck, make his neck even, watch for movement and displacement, and sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 know that this fracture is restored within thirty or forty days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the remedies.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	In the back of the hand and fingers, there are few fractures, but rather many bending multiple times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	 And when the hand's plant is broken or bent, the patient must sit with crossed arms, straight and evenly positioned in front of him.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	 then place his hand on the extended cloth, and stretch out the broken bones with the help of the ministers, aligning them as evenly as possible until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	 And apply the plaster and poultices, if an abscess does not come, then insert a probe according to the size of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	 If the break is at the opening around the abdomen of the plant, make a ball of cloths, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken part.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 Then bind a long piece of cloth, and the probe should be as big as the size of the hand and bind it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, it is necessary to place a splint above and another below in the limb, so that the hand is straightened and bound tightly, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the flow between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	 If the break comes in one of the fingers or at the joints, if it is a nail, make it even as necessary.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	 And bind with the hand and if you see one, insert a small straight probe to lift the break and hold it still.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	 And if the fracture is at another joint, such as in the index or one of the others, align it and lay the limb with the healthy digit that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	 Tie them all together securely, for motion is of value, or you place a splint on it, like a pouch does.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And be careful in the restoration and placement of the abscess heat, and care for what comes there, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	 The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one sees it when it turns forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 And the restoration is that you tie the ligament above the fracture, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	 The patient lies on his back, then each minister extends their ligament equally.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is close to the root of the hip, it may be one of the ligaments towards the knee, and the other ligaments on the opposite side of the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	 If it is near the knee, then the ligaments around the knee should be separated, and the tendons below should be extended.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 Then place the mirrors the bone equal to its two hands, as it should be according to its natural shape, and then place the splint and the ligature, unless an abscess does not come forth.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	 And if there is an abscess, let it heal by itself, then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 The ligature is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	 You must wind the bandage above the fracture and bind it firmly in two or three layers, removing any excess, then bend the leg until the heels come to the root of the knee, and insert the long thread between the calf and the leg, below the groin, and bring the end of the thread up.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	 Then turn towards the leg and thigh and bend it, then put on splints for the break, and place a splint on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	 Use soft fabric cloth of about 8 inches between the leg and thigh to equalize the binding, then begin to bind firmly for three or four times around the splint.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	 and as you move up along the splint, gradually loosen it.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	 Then insert two threads that you put between the leg and thigh, bind three splints above them, then go below the top thread to the joint, until you reach the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 And hold it still in place so that it does not move from its position, then leave it like this, and let there be no abscess or swelling or other such thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	 And if it occurs, dislocate [the joint] and reposition what comes out, as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	 and if there are bone fragments that protrude, they must be pulled out, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	 and if it cannot be pulled out, then the limb must be cut open and the fragment removed.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 and heal [the wound] as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	 Sometimes the thighbone is broken in such a way that rods must be inserted, as in the shoulder or arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 Nevertheless, when restored in this manner, it does not hurt the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is healed within a few days or a little more or less, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee joint occurs little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not really a fracture, but rather a split or piercing, causing pain at every wound and this hurts greatly.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	 And the restoration is that the ends which are rounded are made even with each other, until they are united as much as possible;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	 Then place the arm-band, and put a round stick (if necessary), and hold it as needed, then check all the positions mentioned in other broken places, such as an abscess or similar.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Put to every accident whatever is necessary until it becomes healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	 Know that there are two bones in the leg, of which one is called "mastodon" and the other is called "wolf.
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 And a break in the leg occurs similarly to one in the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the procedures are all the same. If both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the slender bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	 And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well;
et torne desoz.	 and turns underneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	 Then apply extension, make it even, and tie the joints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	 but nevertheless, if the break is misshapen and there are several pieces, the extension should be less and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 align it according to your judgment.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	 And when you have completed your work, take two splints of willow wood that support the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee to below;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	 then wrap both splints around it and bind them in the middle, so that the leg will not be able to bend to the right or left, and thus it is good;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	 And no one applies the bandages to the long part of the leg, and it is fastened with a rod, and they put the leg for restraint from movement, and properly done is this in the break where there is pain.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	 And move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 if it is cured when it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break, but sometimes breaks occur in the bones of the foot and toes, and it requires certain treatment in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	 If there is a bone fracture in the foot break, and you see the bones pushing against each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wants to walk, and now put your foot under his, where the bones are lifted, and then press it until they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 Then place the pillar and stopper on top, and put a small table under the stomach for two hands, then pull it forward, then when you have wrapped cloths around, and other things that you may need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandages, for you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	 And if any of the two are broken, restore them as we have said regarding the hands.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	 Then insert a stick broken in two across the shoulder, and it should be slightly larger, then place beneath the joint that I said, and hold it in place.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	 If there are two or three, or more, break them, then place a stick across each shoulder according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen cloth, and hold the joint under the arm.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 and remain on top of the joint above the belly of the arm, so that it is well covered.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	 And you must not forget the other things I said about other breaks, as I have mentioned.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 Treat each injury as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	 When the natural bone of the female pelvis is broken, make her sit with her back leaning to one side and hold her from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	 Then fill the bladder with the patient's wound linen, also as large as a bull's eye.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	 Then turn the woman and lift her back little by little, and then push the linen until it reaches the opening of the wound, and return the bone to its place with the bull's eye.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	 And when she wants to urinate, remove the linen, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or thereabouts.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	 The break will be healed, and if you see it, take a bladder of goat's skin, attach a tube to it, and insert the entire bladder into the wound.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	 Then blow into the tube forcefully, until the bladder is inflated inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	 Nature will heal the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then fill it with cotton, and leave it for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	 And when the arm bone is broken in a man or woman, restore it as we have said in the thighbone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And these fractures should not be concealed from those who study and practice this art, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	 For fractures indicate in many cases the right path for restoration:
enten le donques.	 Therefore, let us proceed.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	 In the thighbone, when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and insert the thighbone;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 Then wrap fabrics around it, and leave for three days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	for the one who has a breakage with wound, particularly if it is large, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or something similar, that it should be treated now, so that the sores mentioned previously bear witness to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, apply vinegar to it, if you have none else, then begin again to heal the breakage in that same hour, or on that day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes up, wait until the ninth day for it to be soothed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad incident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears exposed on the edge of the wound, you must set it gently in place with light pressure and extend it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	 And if the extension does not present itself for you to make it even with your hands, then straighten it with this tool which is of iron, having seven or eight inches in length, and the width according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	 Also, it is necessary for the mirror that he takes III or IV, according to what he needs in each cure of breaking.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 and be round and somewhat large so that it does not bend at the compression on the member in your work, and be sharp in front, and thick from the middle to the point.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	 And it is called "palanch", which means that the crooked shoulders should be placed on top of the bone appearing at the head.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And push it back once until it returns, and make them even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 If the break is subtle and the instrument cannot properly take hold of the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	 And if you cannot push the bone back, as we have said, use a suitable tool to strike or cut it, be it an instrument for cutting or sawing, at your ability.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 Then reshape the part that is stuck in the bone with sharpness and small scrapes.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is set, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	 Make it return to its place, then wet the linen cloth in black astringent wine, and clean it carefully if it is hot.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	 And do not put any medicine or oil on the wound that would cause rot and corruption to form.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	 Then administer the bandage when you have restored the bone, leave the wound open and cover it all around, according to its size, and be careful that the wound is not constricted by the fracture.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	 And many times have the foolish ones done this, and have brought the sick or dead upon the patient or corroded it once.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 And let the bindings be softer and more pliable than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that a bad event may come to it, as we have said, and you feel pain at the site, do not put needles on it.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 But wrap around [it], instead of needles, hard cloth, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one or two days swelling at the wound, remove whatever you have put on it entirely and apply healing ointment for wounds such as tetrafarmacons and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, once in the morning and once in the evening, as long as it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be aligned in such a manner that the bone moves down gently but gradually.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes many days and cannot heal but the bone keeps moving, since there are small pieces of bone, which is why you should press the wound with pressure, and remove all those dislocated pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula or any kind of corruption comes at the place, you must treat it, according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	 And when the bone is broken and open above the member, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and similar large members, do not draw it out, for many times death comes, but leave it until it can be pulled.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	 By chance, (it) may happen to him after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if possible.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The coming sores on the sore (translated as: 'the sores that come upon a sore')
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	 We often see recovery after the breaking of bones, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a sad sight to see the deformity of the limb.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 And by chance, the limbs cannot perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	 Therefore be careful when we treat him:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	 if you administer medicines that are sticky such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocola, acacia, and similar substances, take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with a sticky wine, or with an abundance of egg white or watercress.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	 And set it on the bed in a basin, and hold it firmly, and do not loosen it for many days.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	 Then dislocate (it), and begin another, until the nodes are removed.
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	 or hold onto a well-made wooden piece.
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	 for the properties of wood are such that it removes all inflammations from limbs.
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	 and if the nodes have turned into hardness, as a stone, it is necessary to remove it, by hitting it from above, and making the excess appear.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 or you scrape it with any shaver, until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb which is weak after being set (or treated)
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	 When the bone fracture has been restored, and remains after limbs weak and delicate, this happens for many reasons.
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	 Because one (the joint) was tied too tightly, and it was not tied as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	 or because there were too many ropes, and the nutriments could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	 porque hay mucha corriente de sangre;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	 For too large movements, not at all in its hour;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 or because it has little blood in its body, it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	 And the treatment consists of making the patient eat, and making the body thin, until the blood is multiplied in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	 and give baths, and give joy and happiness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	 then put the pitch on the member, so that the pitch attracts a great inflammation, and it rots often with cold water, until the inflammation reaches the member;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The member twisted out of health [or order] after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is deformed, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	 Do not believe the foolish who say that one should break a limb completely anew, and many fools have done so in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	 And this practice is condemned, causing great harm, and possibly death by chance.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	 Nevertheless, if the knots and tortures are fresh, it is necessary to loosen them with hot water or softening herbs such as mallow leaves, roots, clover, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	 And make a plaster of mollifying substances, such as darnel well does, and take the root of mallow, steep it in walnut oil or sesame oil, and apply it on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 Take ripe figs made into a paste with wheat bran, and similar medicines that soften the sores.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is opened by rubbing continually and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	 If the tortuosity is hardened and swollen like a stone, and iron treatment is needed, it must be covered up to the bone, and cut through gently with a sharp, thin instrument.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And apply cushions and bandages in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it must now be reset without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	 For if one delays, the joint swells, and there is danger of putting it back to its place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	 Therefore, it is not advisable to move it at dawn when it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	 Often causes spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	 Nevertheless, when this occurs, clean the patient, then let him rest until the abscesses are all appeased.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Then immerse the affected limb in warm water and oil, then gently move it, and treat each member as its treatment is appropriate in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	 It rarely happens that the jaws are dislocated outwards, and the dislocations of both can occur in two ways.
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	 or they are slightly displaced from their places and softened a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the bottom, with saliva pouring from the mouth that it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a small dislocation returns with various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	 And if it is whole and complete, you must quickly reset it without delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	 And in such a manner that the minister holds the head of the patient and pushes one of his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is on two parts.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	 And the other hand must be folded back, to keep it even.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 instruct the patient to soften their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror set even again, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	 And if the reset is difficult (or impossible), especially if both jaws are dislocated together, then anoint them with hot oil and water, until they can be easily reset.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 Do not hide the resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	 And when they are reset equally, and the mouth of the patient closes well, apply a soft cloth made of rose oil and wax, then tie it gently with several threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	 And let the patient sleep on his back, with his arms between two cushions so that he does not move to the right or left, nor exert himself, but take light food until the pain is removed, and the jaws are healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And then eat lightly whatever he desires without exerting himself to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaws are healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be properly set within an hour and are not returned to their places, then fever and accustomed sweats occur, and possibly rupture of the stomach, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	 And when you see this (should be understood as "And if you observe it"), then know that it is destruction.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 and many times the person who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	Of the collarbone
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The collarbone cannot dislocate towards the chest and ribs from the inside, nor can it dislocate outwards; however, it sometimes does dislocate, which is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	 And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back, and extends his arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	 then press the shoulder firmly with your palm, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	 then put on the splint and bind it tightly.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	 and the head of the shoulder should not be dislocated.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	 if it does dislocate again, reset it to its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then put on the splint and bind it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And likewise, the head of the spine is reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The dislocation of the shoulder   (from the previous sentence)
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	 Know that the spine can be dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	 The first way is when it dislocates at the bottom of the neck.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	 and the second one is at the thigh part;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	 and in case of dislocation above, it happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	 do not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate inside for the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	 often dislocate downwards towards the buttocks, especially in those who have little flesh, as it can jump out quickly from there;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 in those who have enough flesh, it jumps out slightly and returns slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men percussion or breaking, and swells the shoulder with an abscess hot, and believes that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	 Therefore, you should test it, as long as you are sure;
et adonques encomence la cure.	 then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	 Dislocations are known when they occur downwards towards the buttocks, and there is a distinction between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find obvious differences between them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	 You will find a hollow in the neck of the shoulder, and press firmly on top of it, as if it were an egg.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	 The patient cannot bring his hand back to its normal position nor make any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	 And if it is dislocated upwards, it should not be hidden, because you can feel it clearly when pressed.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 This kind of dislocation is not difficult to reset when new or if the infant is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	 The method is that the attendant raises the patient's hand upwards, then places his fists beneath it, and forcibly moves the joint upwards to its place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	 The attendant raises the hand and extends it upwards, then places it.
si venra hastanment.	 It will come urgently.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	 If it does not come as we have said within a few hours, then the patient should be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	 and apply a soothing and calming ointment, such as a decoction of elder and fenugreek and melilot in water, and it should be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	 Then the patient should be made to lie on his back, and a piece of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the shoulder. The hand of the patient should be held by an assistant, and the head of the shoulder should be straightened carefully, and the arm of the patient pulled out.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	 And another assistant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	 That shoulder returns immediately, and if you see it dislocated in this manner, reset it accordingly.
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	 and you must be present a person larger than the patient.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	 and he should be on the opposite side of the dislocation, and push the patient's shoulder below the armpit, lift the patient's arm upward so that the patient hangs from it.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 and another servant pulls the patient's hand downward towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too weak, he cannot lift anything heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	 And the dislocation can be reset in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	 and it is that a long needle is placed in the ground, so that the head of the shoulder is as round as a pea, neither too thick nor too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	 then it is placed under the patient, but with padding on top, and the patient should be standing straight.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	 Then extend the hand downwards towards the opposite form, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	 And if it does not return due to everything we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 Take a stick from two arms of great length and four fingers in width, whose head is rounded for easy insertion deep within the anus, following this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	 Then lay the stick's head on a piece of cloth to prevent it from hurting the patient, then insert it into the patient's anus.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	 extend your arms over the stick, and hold the handle of the stick, with your forearm at the end of the arm, then place your hand on a stool of large width, and let your hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 The dislocation comes now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever way that may be, you must place an equal sphere of wool underneath the shoulder, then apply the plaster made of milled powder, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then hold it underneath the shoulder carefully, and twist the linen around the plaster, and bind the hands to their neck, and let them remain in that position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	 It is necessary that he fart a little while the limbs are comforted, for it will heal faster.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	 And then move it more after five or seven days, and move it.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 If it is hardened and not softened, it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture which has come or for some other reason, then you must apply fire cauterization at three points, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	 And if you do all this and it dislocates after seven days, and the jointure does not hold and cannot lift the arm upwards, then understand that the nerve at the base of the shoulder has been severed or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And understand that the jointure will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	 The dislocation that is towards the foot and limbs, or behind, is made by force and extension of hands, and another remedy is administered.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And heal it as long as it remains healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing comes swelling in the member and it gradually moves, then the patient should use baths many times until the swelling subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	The cost of dislocation is...
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	 Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated at points, and at points it returns.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	 and it is dislocated from all parts, both in front and behind, and the dislocation is not put back, for it can be seen clearly and felt.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 and it is dislocated according to each form or shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick body with healthy one, make sure to see them clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is stiff, and cannot bend the arm nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	 And you must reset it in the same way that an abscess comes out, for if an abscess comes out, it would be difficult to reset.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	 And by chance it cannot be put back entirely in all places, especially when it is at the back.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 It is better than other dislocations and it causes greater pain, and by chance death may come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	 And the restoration is such, when it can be returned, that you extend your hand to both of yours;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 and the arms be spread, and the hands to the mirror according to the measurement around, above and below, and push the joint together at their peaks or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and bend the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	 and if it does not want to return to its place, then administer a strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	 and it is that the two ministers extend the arm and mark it with the two ministers so that it does not move in extension.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	 then turn the arm from each side, then when you have wrapped a double-length and wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	 And when the doctor joins the joint with his hand, he should oil it to soften the joint, then push the joint back into place until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And when it is in its place, put on a plaster of dry ointment with egg white, and hold it in place, and fasten the arm to the patient's neck for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	 And if the joint is firm in its place, remove the ligature and leave it be;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	 And if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the plaster and ligature, and leave it in this state for some days until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	 Then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	 And if it feels pain after the reset of the joint, and it becomes motionless, wash and rub it well, and press until it is soothed.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	 Place a fat sheep's wool on the joint, leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and make it enter water.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	 And when it bleeds, wipe the joint gently, then place the wool back on, and then make it enter water again.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this two or three times until it is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	 If you see, place warm damp sheep's wool with butter on it and hold it there.
si revenra a sa disposition.	 It will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	 The joint of the hand dislocates easily, more than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 Immediately, it must be returned to its place, in the same hour that it is dislocated, unless the joint is swollen or there is an abscess hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	 And the resetting is that you put the patient's hand on a table, extend your fingers, and place the eyes so they are even, with the palm over the appearance of the joint, and push until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	 Indeed, you must look if it is in its place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 Then place the patient's hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on the table, and have them put their other hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	 If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If not, press down with plasters to soothe abscesses, and let it rest in that condition.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	 And if it cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in place after any days, then the dislocation persists;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	 The patient must not move his hand as long as it is paralyzed and cannot exert any strength:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	 Therefore know that the nerves or the arteries have been cut:
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 There is no other remedy but to use fire cautery for this case, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at its place, put on the plaster as we have said, then strain it and leave for 5 days, then release and let it rest.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move properly and there is no swelling, wet with warm water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	 Sometimes the thumb of the hand is dislocated on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly:
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	 Then place the thumb and push the dislocation back into its socket until it comes back, then hold the head of the thumb, and pull it towards the side where it is disjointed:
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	 Leave it for two days, then equalize it on that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	 Then loosen it if necessary, as we have said, and dislocate it for a day, make it move, and reattach it after that.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this often, until it is narrowed, and do the same if it dislocates from the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 And do the same when it dislocates from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	And also for the dislocation of the vertebra in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra in the back or neck is dislocated, and if there are multiple dislocations without any treatment, death quickly comes to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	 The signs are that the excretion jumps involuntarily and cannot be held, and many times a member becomes swollen, either the two knees or both arms or the head.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	 And many times the spleen becomes silent in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	 That which becomes silent at the backside is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	 The cure is that you inspect if the gilbositez has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 if it has not had any treatment or healing throughout.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	 And that which comes from falling or blows, or similar things, the old ways of healing said in great words, there was no benefit in all this.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 but I have condensed it according to my intention and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	 I say that in the case of the gilbositez which comes in front, there is no remedy or healing.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	 and similarly that which comes directly to the side, and can be cured only by the one which comes at the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	 And it is that the patient should be extended on his face in a flat position and have something held under him to prevent him from bleeding.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	 Then stick the torch into the patient's head, on the ground, and tie a thread beneath the patient's elbows, ankles, knees, and wrists.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	 and two assistants know the ropes, one at the head and the others at the feet, between the two torches.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 And both torches should be firmly pressed as we have said, and the mirrors place their palms on the spine formed until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	 And if it does not return by this cure, take a board three feet long and curved at the bottom, place the patient on his side, and press the top of the board against the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	 And place the mirror on top of the other head of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if you see, do as the treadle which turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	 And it is that you insert two thongs on the head of the patient from one arm, and between each thong, inside and outside, there should be a palm's breadth of space.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	 And let each thong have the pivot where the treadle moves, and let the thongs be firmly in the ground so that they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	 And between each of the two thongs, there should be another rotating thong, as in gears, and have two small thongs of a palm's length for turning the treadle.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And then tie the tendon that is among the ankles towards the neck, and the other tendon towards the feet at the other neck, and each of the ministers turns his neck to the entire tendon, and the masters align the spine equally as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when it is aligned, put a drying plaster with egg on top, then bandage, and then the cast made of a board three feet long, which takes care of the swelling and the part of the spine, then tie a rope as we have said, use the patient with gentle treatment until he is well.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	 And if anything comes at the end of his health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines with the bandage that we have said before;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	 And sometimes they administer a piece of wood, and sometimes the appearance comes at the lower part of the spondylus (spine), and it is thought to be a dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	 And that is the bone opening, so one should not have any presumption.
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 By accident it may bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of the dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	 Know that the joints of the neck and shoulder come apart only through dislocations, not like other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	 And the joint of the neck is dislocated in four parts.
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	 Inside and outside, front and back.
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Further inside it is more dislocated, but less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	 And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when the diseased leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased joints open wider than those of the healthy, and the diseased cannot bend their knee in fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And it is the joint that is swollen with abscess heat, because the shoulder of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes to discharge (or expel), is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	 And the signs of this condition on the front part are that they should stretch out their leg according to fulfillment.
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 In any case, the knee should not double in pain and if one wishes to make it walk, it cannot do so beforehand, and it holds back its urine, and the ankle swells up and when it walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one whose condition is behind (or posterior), are that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and the leg is twisted more than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	 The recurrences of this dislocation-like appearance are that you observe whether the dislocation is old and remains in its position without any cure.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 And it should not be that there is any presumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	 And in the one where the dislocation is fresh, and this is one of four types of dislocation, hurry up that you return the joint, and push it inward and outward, and move it left and right;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 Perhaps it will return on its own and does not require any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must apply a strong splint and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or tie it to the thigh using a bandage.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	 and another helper extends his hand over it in such a manner that he pushes his hands underneath the knees, then ties it with a strong bandage around the calf.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	 and another one ties the head with the bandage;
